        <td style="text-align:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia#List_of_federal_subjects" title="Federal subjects of Russia">
          82nd
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr class="mergedtoprow">

         </b>
         (2017 est.)
        </td>

      <p>
       <b>
        Saint Petersburg
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru">
        Санкт-Петербу́рг
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">
         tr.
        </a>
       </small>
       <i>
        <span lang="ru-Latn">
         Sankt-Peterburg
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <small>
        IPA:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">
         [ˈsankt pʲɪtʲɪrˈburk]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small class="nowrap">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Ru-Sankt_Peterburg_Leningrad_Petrograd_Piter.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/Ru-Sankt_Peterburg_Leningrad_Petrograd_Piter.ogg" title="Ru-Sankt Peterburg Leningrad Petrograd Piter.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       ) is Russia's
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Russia_by_population" title="List of cities and towns in Russia by population">
        second-largest city
       </a>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">
        Moscow
       </a>
       , with five million inhabitants in 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Census_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010Census-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An important Russian
       <a href="/wiki/Ports_of_the_Baltic_Sea" title="Ports of the Baltic Sea">
        port on the Baltic Sea
       </a>
       , it has a status of a
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">
        federal subject
       </a>
       (a
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">
        federal city
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Situated on the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_River" title="Neva River">
        Neva River
       </a>
       , at the head of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">
        Gulf of Finland
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       , it was founded by
       <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">
        Tsar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">
        Peter the Great
       </a>
       on May 27 [
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">
        O.S.
       </a>
       16] 1703. In 1914, the name was changed from Saint Petersburg to
       <b>
        Petrograd
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru">
        Петрогра́д
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        IPA:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">
         [pʲɪtrɐˈgrat]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), in 1924 to
       <b>
        Leningrad
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru">
        Ленингра́д
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        IPA:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">
         [lʲɪnʲɪnˈgrat]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), and in 1991 back to Saint Petersburg. Between 1713 and 1728 and in 1732–1918, Saint Petersburg was the capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        imperial Russia
       </a>
       . In 1918, the central government bodies moved to Moscow.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McColl_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-McColl-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is one of the modern cities of Russia, as well as its cultural capital.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Historic_Centre_of_Saint_Petersburg_and_Related_Groups_of_Monuments" title="Historic Centre of Saint Petersburg and Related Groups of Monuments">
        Historic Centre of Saint Petersburg and Related Groups of Monuments
       </a>
       constitute a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        UNESCO World Heritage Site
       </a>
       . Saint Petersburg is home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">
        Hermitage
       </a>
       , one of the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">
        art museums
       </a>
       in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_consulates_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="List of consulates in Saint Petersburg">
        foreign consulates
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">
        international corporations
       </a>
       , banks and businesses have offices in Saint Petersburg.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
        Name
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       An admirer of everything Dutch, Peter the Great originally named the city,
       <b>
        Sankt-Peterburg
       </b>
       [Санкт-Петербург] -- which lacked the letter "s" between "Peter" and "burg".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On Sept. 1, 1914, after the outbreak of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       , the Imperial government renamed the city
       <b>
        Petrograd
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru">
        Петрогра́д
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        IPA:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">
         [pʲɪtrɐˈgrat]
        </a>
       </span>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       meaning "Peter's City", in order to expunge the German-sounding words
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Sankt#German" title="wikt:Sankt">
         Sankt
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Burg#German" title="wikt:Burg">
         Burg
        </a>
       </i>
       . On 26 January 1924 it was renamed to
       <b>
        Leningrad
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru">
        Ленингра́д
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        IPA:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">
         [lʲɪnʲɪnˈgrat]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), meaning "Lenin's City". On 6 September 1991, the original name, Sankt-Peterburg, was returned. Today, in English the city is known as "St. Petersburg." Local residents often refer to the city by its nickname,
       <b>
        Piter
       </b>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>

        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">

           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>

            (January 2011)
           </i>

      <h3>
       <span id="Imperial_Era_.281703.E2.80.931917.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Era_(1703–1917)">
        Imperial Era (1703–1917)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Imperial Era (1703–1917)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg/220px-Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg/330px-Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg/440px-Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bronze_Horseman_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Horseman" title="Bronze Horseman">
          Bronze Horseman
         </a>
         , monument to Peter the Great
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Swedish colonists built
       <a href="/wiki/Nyenschantz" title="Nyenschantz">
        Nyenskans
       </a>
       , a fortress at the mouth of the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_River" title="Neva River">
        Neva River
       </a>
       in 1611, in what was then called
       <a href="/wiki/Ingria" title="Ingria">
        Ingermanland
       </a>
       , which was inhabited by
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Finns" title="Baltic Finns">
        Finnic
       </a>
       tribe of
       <a href="/wiki/Ingrian_Finns" title="Ingrian Finns">
        Ingrians
       </a>
       . The small town of Nyen grew up around it.
      </p>
      <p>
       At the end of the 17th century, Peter the Great, who was very interested in seafaring and maritime affairs, wanted Russia to gain a seaport in order to trade with Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wilson82_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wilson82-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He needed a better seaport than the country's main one at the time,
       <a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk" title="Arkhangelsk">
        Arkhangelsk
       </a>
       , which was on the
       <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">
        White Sea
       </a>
       in the far north and closed to shipping during the winter.
      </p>
      <p>
       On May 12 [
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">
        O.S.
       </a>
       1] 1703, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">
        Great Northern War
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">
        Peter the Great
       </a>
       captured Nyenskans
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and soon replaced the fortress. On May 27 [
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">
        O.S.
       </a>
       16] 1703,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes66_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hughes66-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       closer to the
       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">
        estuary
       </a>
       5 km (3 mi) inland from the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">
        gulf
       </a>
       ), on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zayachy_Island" title="Zayachy Island">
        Zayachy (Hare) Island
       </a>
       , he laid down the
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Fortress" title="Peter and Paul Fortress">
        Peter and Paul Fortress
       </a>
       , which became the first brick and stone building of the new city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spenc_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-spenc-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city was built by
       <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">
        conscripted peasants
       </a>
       from all over Russia; a number of Swedish
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/POWs" title="POWs">
        prisoners of war
       </a>
       were also involved in some years
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       under the supervision of
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Danilovich_Menshikov" title="Alexander Danilovich Menshikov">
        Alexander Menshikov
       </a>
       . Tens of thousands of serfs died building the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Later, the city became the centre of the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Governorate" title="Saint Petersburg Governorate">
        Saint Petersburg Governorate
       </a>
       . Peter moved the capital from Moscow to Saint Petersburg in 1712, 9 years before the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nystad" title="Treaty of Nystad">
        Treaty of Nystad
       </a>
       of 1721 ended the war; he referred to Saint Petersburg as the capital (or seat of government) as early as 1704.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wilson82_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-wilson82-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_spb_1744_high.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1448" data-file-width="2100" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Map_spb_1744_high.jpg/260px-Map_spb_1744_high.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Map_spb_1744_high.jpg/390px-Map_spb_1744_high.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Map_spb_1744_high.jpg/520px-Map_spb_1744_high.jpg 2x" width="260"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_spb_1744_high.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Saint Petersburg, 1744
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During its first few years, the city developed around Trinity Square on the right bank of the Neva, near the Peter and Paul Fortress. However, Saint Petersburg soon started to be built out according to a plan. By 1716 the
       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Italian" title="Swiss Italian">
        Swiss Italian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Trezzini" title="Domenico Trezzini">
        Domenico Trezzini
       </a>
       had elaborated a project whereby the city centre would be located on
       <a href="/wiki/Vasilyevsky_Island" title="Vasilyevsky Island">
        Vasilyevsky Island
       </a>
       and shaped by a rectangular grid of canals. The project was not completed, but is evident in the layout of the streets. In 1716, Peter the Great appointed Frenchman
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Alexandre_Le_Blond" title="Jean-Baptiste Alexandre Le Blond">
        Jean-Baptiste Alexandre Le Blond
       </a>
       as the
       <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">
        chief architect
       </a>
       of Saint Petersburg.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The style of
       <a href="/wiki/Petrine_Baroque" title="Petrine Baroque">
        Petrine Baroque
       </a>
       , developed by Trezzini and other architects and exemplified by such buildings as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Menshikov_Palace" title="Menshikov Palace">
        Menshikov Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kunstkamera" title="Kunstkamera">
        Kunstkamera
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Cathedral" title="Peter and Paul Cathedral">
        Peter and Paul Cathedral
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Collegia" title="Twelve Collegia">
        Twelve Collegia
       </a>
       , became prominent in the city architecture of the early 18th century. In 1724 the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">
        Academy of Sciences
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University" title="Saint Petersburg State University">
        University
       </a>
       and Academic Gymnasium were established in Saint Petersburg by Peter the Great.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1725, Peter died at the age of fifty-two. His endeavours to modernize Russia had met with opposition from the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_nobility" title="Russian nobility">
        Russian nobility
       </a>
       —resulting in several attempts on his life and a treason case involving his son.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1728,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_II_of_Russia" title="Peter II of Russia">
        Peter II of Russia
       </a>
       moved his seat back to Moscow. But four years later, in 1732, under Empress
       <a href="/wiki/Anna_of_Russia" title="Anna of Russia">
        Anna of Russia
       </a>
       , Saint Petersburg was again designated as the capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian Empire
       </a>
       . It remained the seat of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanov_dynasty" title="Romanov dynasty">
        Romanov dynasty
       </a>
       and the Imperial Court of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Tsars" title="Russian Tsars">
        Russian Tsars
       </a>
       , as well as the seat of the Russian government, for another 186 years until the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">
        communist revolution of 1917
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1736–1737 the city suffered from catastrophic fires. To rebuild the damaged boroughs, a committee under
       <a href="/wiki/Burkhard_Christoph_von_M%C3%BCnnich" title="Burkhard Christoph von Münnich">
        Burkhard Christoph von Münnich
       </a>
       commissioned a new plan in 1737. The city was divided into five boroughs, and the city center was moved to the Admiralty borough, situated on the east bank between the Neva and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fontanka" title="Fontanka">
        Fontanka
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG/220px-%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG/330px-%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG/440px-%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%86%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%89%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%8C_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D0%B8%D0%B7_%D0%AD%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0..JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Palace_Square" title="Palace Square">
          Palace Square
         </a>
         backed by the
         <a href="/wiki/General_Staff_Building_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="General Staff Building (Saint Petersburg)">
          General staff arch and building
         </a>
         , as the main square of the Russian Empire it was the setting of many events of historic significance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       It developed along three radial streets, which meet at the
       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_building,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Admiralty building, Saint Petersburg">
        Admiralty building
       </a>
       and are now one street known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nevsky_Prospekt" title="Nevsky Prospekt">
        Nevsky Prospekt
       </a>
       (which is considered the main street of the city),
       <a href="/wiki/Gorokhovaya_Street" title="Gorokhovaya Street">
        Gorokhovaya Street
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voznesensky_Prospekt" title="Voznesensky Prospekt">
        Voznesensky Prospekt
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">
        Baroque architecture
       </a>
       became dominant in the city during the first sixty years, culminating in the Elizabethan Baroque, represented most notably by Italian
       <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Bartolomeo_Rastrelli" title="Francesco Bartolomeo Rastrelli">
        Bartolomeo Rastrelli
       </a>
       with such buildings as the
       <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">
        Winter Palace
       </a>
       . In the 1760s, Baroque architecture was succeeded by
       <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">
        neoclassical architecture
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Established in 1762, the Commission of Stone Buildings of Moscow and Saint Petersburg ruled that no structure in the city can be higher than the Winter Palace and prohibited spacing between buildings. During the reign of
       <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">
        Catherine the Great
       </a>
       in the 1760s–1780s, the banks of the Neva were lined with
       <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">
        granite
       </a>
       embankments.
      </p>
      <p>
       However, it was not until 1850 that the first permanent bridge across the Neva,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blagoveshchensky_Bridge" title="Blagoveshchensky Bridge">
        Blagoveshchensky Bridge
       </a>
       , was allowed to open. Before that, only
       <a href="/wiki/Pontoon_bridge" title="Pontoon bridge">
        pontoon bridges
       </a>
       were allowed.
       <a href="/wiki/Obvodny_Canal" title="Obvodny Canal">
        Obvodny Canal
       </a>
       (dug in 1769–1833) became the southern limit of the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       The most prominent neoclassical and
       <a href="/wiki/Empire_style" title="Empire style">
        Empire-style
       </a>
       architects in Saint Petersburg included:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Vallin_de_la_Mothe" title="Jean-Baptiste Vallin de la Mothe">
         Jean-Baptiste Vallin de la Mothe
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Academy_of_Arts" title="Imperial Academy of Arts">
         Imperial Academy of Arts
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">
         Small Hermitage
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Great_Gostiny_Dvor" title="Great Gostiny Dvor">
         Gostiny Dvor
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_Island" title="New Holland Island">
         New Holland Arch
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_of_St._Catherine_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Catholic Church of St. Catherine (Saint Petersburg)">
         Catholic Church of St. Catherine
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Rinaldi_(architect)" title="Antonio Rinaldi (architect)">
         Antonio Rinaldi
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Marble_Palace" title="Marble Palace">
         Marble Palace
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Yury_Felten" title="Yury Felten">
         Yury Felten
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">
         Old Hermitage
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Chesme_Church" title="Chesme Church">
         Chesme Church
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Quarenghi" title="Giacomo Quarenghi">
         Giacomo Quarenghi
        </a>
        (Academy of Sciences,
        <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Theatre" title="Hermitage Theatre">
         Hermitage Theatre
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Moika_Palace" title="Moika Palace">
         Yusupov Palace
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Voronikhin" title="Andrey Voronikhin">
         Andrey Voronikhin
        </a>
        (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Mining_Institute" title="Saint Petersburg Mining Institute">
         Mining Institute
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazan_Cathedral,_St._Petersburg" title="Kazan Cathedral, St. Petersburg">
         Kazan Cathedral
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Andreyan_Zakharov" title="Andreyan Zakharov">
         Andreyan Zakharov
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_building,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Admiralty building, Saint Petersburg">
         Admiralty building
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_Thomas_de_Thomon" title="Jean-François Thomas de Thomon">
         Jean-François Thomas de Thomon
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Old_Saint_Petersburg_Stock_Exchange_and_Rostral_Columns" title="Old Saint Petersburg Stock Exchange and Rostral Columns">
         Spit of Vasilievsky Island
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Rossi_(architect)" title="Carlo Rossi (architect)">
         Carlo Rossi
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Yelagin_Palace" title="Yelagin Palace">
         Yelagin Palace
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">
         Mikhailovsky Palace
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Alexandrinsky_Theatre" title="Alexandrinsky Theatre">
         Alexandrine Theatre
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Senate_Square_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Senate Square (Saint Petersburg)">
         Senate and Synod Buildings
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/General_Staff_Building_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="General Staff Building (Saint Petersburg)">
         General staff Building
        </a>
        , design of many streets and squares)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Stasov" title="Vasily Stasov">
         Vasily Stasov
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Triumphal_Gate" title="Moscow Triumphal Gate">
         Moscow Triumphal Gate
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Cathedral,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Trinity Cathedral, Saint Petersburg">
         Trinity Cathedral
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Auguste_de_Montferrand" title="Auguste de Montferrand">
         Auguste de Montferrand
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Isaac's Cathedral">
         Saint Isaac's Cathedral
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Column" title="Alexander Column">
         Alexander Column
        </a>
        )
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kolman_decembrists.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="434" data-file-width="640" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kolman_decembrists.jpg/220px-Kolman_decembrists.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kolman_decembrists.jpg/330px-Kolman_decembrists.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kolman_decembrists.jpg/440px-Kolman_decembrists.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kolman_decembrists.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decembrists" title="Decembrists">
          Decembrists
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/Senate_Square_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Senate Square (Saint Petersburg)">
          Senate Square
         </a>
         , December 26, 1825.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1810,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">
        Alexander I
       </a>
       established the first engineering
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higher_learning_institution" title="Higher learning institution">
        Higher learning institution
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Military_Engineering-Technical_University" title="Military Engineering-Technical University">
        Saint Petersburg Main military engineering School
       </a>
       in Saint Petersburg. Many monuments commemorate the Russian victory over
       <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">
        Napoleonic France
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia" title="French invasion of Russia">
        Patriotic War of 1812
       </a>
       , including the
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Column" title="Alexander Column">
        Alexander Column
       </a>
       by Montferrand, erected in 1834, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narva_Triumphal_Gate" title="Narva Triumphal Gate">
        Narva Triumphal Gate
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1825, the suppressed
       <a href="/wiki/Decembrist_revolt" title="Decembrist revolt">
        Decembrist revolt
       </a>
       against
       <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia" title="Nicholas I of Russia">
        Nicholas I
       </a>
       took place on the
       <a href="/wiki/Senate_Square_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Senate Square (Saint Petersburg)">
        Senate Square
       </a>
       in the city, a day after Nicholas assumed the throne.
      </p>
      <p>
       By the 1840s, neoclassical architecture had given way to various romanticist styles, which dominated until the 1890s, represented by such architects as
       <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Stackenschneider" title="Andrei Stackenschneider">
        Andrei Stackenschneider
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Mariinsky_Palace" title="Mariinsky Palace">
        Mariinsky Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Beloselsky-Belozersky_Palace" title="Beloselsky-Belozersky Palace">
        Beloselsky-Belozersky Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Palace" title="Nicholas Palace">
        Nicholas Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Stackenschneider" title="Andrei Stackenschneider">
        New Michael Palace
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Thon" title="Konstantin Thon">
        Konstantin Thon
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Moskovsky_railway_station_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Moskovsky railway station (Saint Petersburg)">
        Moskovsky railway station
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       With the
       <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_reform_of_1861" title="Emancipation reform of 1861">
        emancipation of the serfs
       </a>
       undertaken by
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia" title="Alexander II of Russia">
        Alexander II
       </a>
       in 1861 and an
       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">
        Industrial Revolution
       </a>
       , the influx of former peasants into the capital increased greatly. Poor boroughs spontaneously emerged on the outskirts of the city. Saint Petersburg surpassed Moscow in population and industrial growth; it developed as one of the largest industrial cities in Europe, with a major naval base (in
       <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">
        Kronstadt
       </a>
       ), river and sea port.
      </p>
      <p>
       The names of saints
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">
        Peter
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Paul" title="Saint Paul">
        Paul
       </a>
       , bestowed upon
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Fortress" title="Peter and Paul Fortress">
        original city's citadel
       </a>
       and its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Cathedral" title="Peter and Paul Cathedral">
        cathedral
       </a>
       (from 1725—a
       <a href="/wiki/Burial_vault_(tomb)" title="Burial vault (tomb)">
        burial vault
       </a>
       of Russian emperors) coincidentally were the names of the first two assassinated Russian Emperors,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Russia" title="Peter III of Russia">
        Peter III
       </a>
       (1762, supposedly killed in a conspiracy led by his wife,
       <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">
        Catherine the Great
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">
        Paul I
       </a>
       (1801,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nicholas_Zubov" title="Nicholas Zubov">
        Nicholas Zubov
       </a>
       and other conspirators who brought to power
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">
        Alexander I
       </a>
       , the son of their victim). The third emperor's assassination took place in Petersburg in 1881 when
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia" title="Alexander II of Russia">
        Alexander II
       </a>
       fell victim to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narodniki" title="Narodniki">
        narodniki
       </a>
       (see the
       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Savior_on_Blood" title="Church of the Savior on Blood">
        Church of the Savior on Blood
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

          </div>

       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">

           </a>
          </p>

       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">

           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 183.33333333333px">
        <div style="width: 183.33333333333px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 181.33333333333px;">

           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">

           <a href="/wiki/Petergof" title="Petergof">

           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution" title="1905 Russian Revolution">
        Revolution of 1905
       </a>
       began in Saint Petersburg and spread rapidly into the provinces.
      </p>
      <p>
       On September 1, 1914, after the outbreak of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       , the Imperial government renamed the city
       <i>
        Petrograd
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       meaning "Peter's City", to remove the German words
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Sankt#German" title="wikt:Sankt">
         Sankt
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Burg#German" title="wikt:Burg">
         Burg
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Revolution_and_Soviet_Era_.281917.E2.80.931941.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Revolution_and_Soviet_Era_(1917–1941)">
        Revolution and Soviet Era (1917–1941)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Revolution and Soviet Era (1917–1941)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In March 1917, during the
       <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">
        February Revolution
       </a>
       Nicholas II abdicated both for himself and on behalf of his son, ending the Russian monarchy and over three hundred years of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romanov_dynasty" title="Romanov dynasty">
        Romanov
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dynastic_rule" title="Dynastic rule">
        dynastic rule
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="573" data-file-width="973" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png/220px-Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png/330px-Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png/440px-Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Desfile-uno-mayo-II--rusia--russianbolshevik00rossuoft.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1917" title="Russian Revolution of 1917">
          Russian Revolution of 1917
         </a>
         began in Petrograd when the
         <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">
          Bolsheviks
         </a>
         stormed the
         <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">
          Winter Palace
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On November 7, 1917 (
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">
        OS
       </a>
       October 25), the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik" title="Bolshevik">
        Bolsheviks
       </a>
       , led by
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">
        Vladimir Lenin
       </a>
       , stormed the
       <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">
        Winter Palace
       </a>
       in an event known thereafter as the
       <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">
        October Revolution
       </a>
       , which led to the end of the post-Tsarist
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">
        provisional government
       </a>
       , the transfer of all political power to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Worker%27s_council" title="Worker's council">
        Soviets
       </a>
       , and the rise of the
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">
        Communist Party
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After that the city acquired a new descriptive name, "the city of three revolutions",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-russia-travel_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-russia-travel-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       referring to the three major developments in the political history of Russia of the early 20th-century.
      </p>
      <p>
       In September and October 1917, German troops
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Albion" title="Operation Albion">
        invaded
       </a>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Estonian_archipelago" title="West Estonian archipelago">
        West Estonian archipelago
       </a>
       and threatened Petrograd with bombardment and invasion. On March 12, 1918, the Soviets transferred the government to Moscow, to keep it away from the state border. During the ensuing
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">
        Civil War
       </a>
       , in 1919 general
       <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Yudenich" title="Nikolai Yudenich">
        Yudenich
       </a>
       advancing from Estonia repeated the attempt to capture the city, but
       <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">
        Leon Trotsky
       </a>
       mobilized the army and forced him to retreat.
      </p>
      <p>
       On January 26, 1924, five days after Lenin's death, Petrograd was renamed
       <i>
        Leningrad
       </i>
       . Later some streets and other
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/toponym" title="wiktionary:toponym">
        toponyms
       </a>
       were renamed accordingly. The city has over 230 places associated with the life and activities of Lenin. Some of them were turned into museums,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kann_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kann-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_cruiser_Aurora" title="Russian cruiser Aurora">
        cruiser
        <i>
         Aurora
        </i>
       </a>
       – a symbol of the October Revolution and the oldest ship in the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Navy" title="Russian Navy">
        Russian Navy
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1920s and 1930s, the poor outskirts were reconstructed into regularly planned boroughs.
       <a href="/wiki/Constructivist_architecture" title="Constructivist architecture">
        Constructivist architecture
       </a>
       flourished around that time. Housing became a government-provided
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_utility" title="Social utility">
        amenity
       </a>
       ; many "bourgeois" apartments were so large that numerous families were assigned to what were called "communal" apartments (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kommunal_apartment" title="Kommunal apartment">
         kommunalkas
        </a>
       </i>
       ). By the 1930s, 68% of the population lived in such housing. In 1935 a new general plan was outlined, whereby the city should expand to the south. Constructivism was rejected in favor of a more pompous
       <a href="/wiki/Stalinist_architecture" title="Stalinist architecture">
        Stalinist architecture
       </a>
       . Moving the city center further from the border with Finland,
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">
        Stalin
       </a>
       adopted a plan to build a new city hall with a huge adjacent square at the southern end of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskovsky_Prospekt" title="Moskovsky Prospekt">
        Moskovsky Prospekt
       </a>
       , designated as the new main street of Leningrad. After the Winter (Soviet-Finnish) war 1939-1940, the Soviet-Finnish border moved northwards. Nevsky Prospekt with Palace Square maintained the functions and the role of a city center.
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 1931, Leningrad was administratively separated from
       <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast" title="Leningrad Oblast">
        Leningrad Oblast
       </a>
       . At that time it included the Leningrad Suburban District, some parts of which were transferred back to Leningrad Oblast in 1936 and turned into
       <a href="/wiki/Vsevolozhsky_District" title="Vsevolozhsky District">
        Vsevolozhsky District
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Krasnoselsky_District,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Krasnoselsky District, Saint Petersburg">
        Krasnoselsky District
       </a>
       , Pargolovsky District and Slutsky District (renamed Pavlovsky District in 1944).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On December 1, 1934,
       <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Kirov" title="Sergey Kirov">
        Sergey Kirov
       </a>
       , the popular communist leader of Leningrad, was assassinated, which became the pretext for the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">
        Great Purge
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="World_War_II_.281941.E2.80.931945.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_(1941–1945)">
        World War II (1941–1945)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: World War II (1941–1945)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">
        Siege of Leningrad
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="366" data-file-width="600" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_2153_After_bombing.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Citizens of Leningrad during the 872-day
         <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">
          siege
         </a>
         , in which more than one million civilians died, mostly from starvation.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        German forces
       </a>
       besieged Leningrad following the Axis invasion of the Soviet Union in June 1941.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The siege lasted 872 days, or almost two and a half years,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       from September 8, 1941 to January 27, 1944.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">
        Siege of Leningrad
       </a>
       proved one of the longest, most destructive, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Most_lethal_battles_in_world_history#Sieges_and_urban_combat" title="Most lethal battles in world history">
        most lethal sieges
       </a>
       of a major city in
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">
        modern history
       </a>
       . It isolated the city from food supplies except those provided through the
       <a href="/wiki/Road_of_Life" title="Road of Life">
        Road of Life
       </a>
       across
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ladoga" title="Lake Ladoga">
        Lake Ladoga
       </a>
       , which could not make it through until the lake literally froze. More than one million civilians were killed, mainly from starvation. Many others were eventually evacuated or escaped, so the city became largely depopulated.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On May 1, 1945
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">
        Joseph Stalin
       </a>
       , in his Supreme Commander Order No. 20, named Leningrad, alongside
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stalingrad" title="Stalingrad">
        Stalingrad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">
        Sevastopol
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">
        Odessa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hero_City" title="Hero City">
        hero cities
       </a>
       of the war. A law acknowledging the honorary title of "Hero City" passed on May 8, 1965 (the 20th anniversary of the victory in the Great Patriotic War), during the
       <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">
        Brezhnev era
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Presidium_of_the_Supreme_Soviet" title="Presidium of the Supreme Soviet">
        Presidium of the Supreme Soviet
       </a>
       of the USSR awarded Leningrad as a Hero City the
       <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Lenin" title="Order of Lenin">
        Order of Lenin
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_Star_medal" title="Gold Star medal">
        Gold Star medal
       </a>
       "for the heroic resistance of the city and tenacity of the survivors of the Siege". The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hero-City_Obelisk" title="Hero-City Obelisk">
        Hero-City Obelisk
       </a>
       bearing the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_Star_medal" title="Gold Star medal">
        Gold Star sign
       </a>
       was installed in April 1985.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Soviet_Era_Continued_.281945.E2.80.931991.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Era_Continued_(1945–1991)">
        Soviet Era Continued (1945–1991)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Soviet Era Continued (1945–1991)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In October 1946 some territories along the northern coast of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">
        Gulf of Finland
       </a>
       , which had passed to the USSR from Finland in 1940 under the
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Peace_Treaty" title="Moscow Peace Treaty">
        peace treaty
       </a>
       following the
       <a href="/wiki/Winter_War" title="Winter War">
        Winter War
       </a>
       , were transferred from Leningrad Oblast to Leningrad and divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Sestroretsk" title="Sestroretsk">
        Sestroretsky District
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kurortny_District" title="Kurortny District">
        Kurortny District
       </a>
       . These included the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Zelenogorsk,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Zelenogorsk, Saint Petersburg">
        Terijoki
       </a>
       (renamed
       <a href="/wiki/Zelenogorsk" title="Zelenogorsk">
        Zelenogorsk
       </a>
       in 1948).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Leningrad and many of its suburbs were rebuilt over the post-war decades, partially according to pre-war plans. The 1948 general plan for Leningrad featured radial
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">
        urban development
       </a>
       in the north as well as in the south. In 1953
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pavlovsky_District,_Leningrad_Oblast&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pavlovsky District, Leningrad Oblast (page does not exist)">
        Pavlovsky District
       </a>
       in Leningrad Oblast was abolished, and parts of its territory, including Pavlovsk, merged with Leningrad. In 1954 the settlements
       <a href="/wiki/Levashovo,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Levashovo, Saint Petersburg">
        Levashovo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pargolovo" title="Pargolovo">
        Pargolovo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pesochny,_Russia" title="Pesochny, Russia">
        Pesochny
       </a>
       merged with Leningrad.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Leningrad gave its name to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leningrad_Affair" title="Leningrad Affair">
        Leningrad Affair
       </a>
       (1949–1952), a notable event in the postwar political struggle in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">
        USSR
       </a>
       . It was a product of rivalry between Stalin's potential successors where one side was represented by the leaders of the city
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">
        Communist Party
       </a>
       organization—the second most significant one in the country after Moscow. The entire elite leadership of Leningrad was destroyed, including the former mayor
       <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Kuznetsov" title="Alexey Kuznetsov">
        Kuznetsov
       </a>
       , the acting mayor Pyotr Sergeevich Popkov, and all their deputies; overall 23 leaders were sentenced to the death penalty, 181 to prison or exile (exonerated in 1954). About 2,000 ranking officials across the USSR were expelled from the party and the Komsomol and removed from leadership positions. They were accused (almost entirely falsely) of Russian
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">
        nationalism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zubkova_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Zubkova-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Metro" title="Saint Petersburg Metro">
        Leningrad Metro
       </a>
       underground
       <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">
        rapid transit system
       </a>
       , designed before the war, opened in 1955 with its first eight stations decorated with
       <a href="/wiki/Marble" title="Marble">
        marble
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze" title="Bronze">
        bronze
       </a>
       . However, after the death of Stalin in 1953, the perceived ornamental excesses of the Stalinist architecture were abandoned. From the 1960s to the 1980s many new residential boroughs were built on the outskirts; while the
       <a href="/wiki/Functionalism_(architecture)" title="Functionalism (architecture)">
        functionalist
       </a>
       apartment blocks were nearly identical to each other, many families moved there from
       <i>
        kommunalkas
       </i>
       in the city centre in order to live in separate apartments.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Contemporary_Era_.281991-present.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_Era_(1991-present)">
        Contemporary Era (1991-present)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Contemporary Era (1991-present)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2662" data-file-width="4213" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg/220px-Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg/330px-Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg/440px-Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spb_Views_from_Isaac_Cathedral_May2012_09.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View from the Colonnade, St. Isaac's Cathedral, Saint Petersburg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On June 12, 1991, simultaneously with the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_presidential_election,_1991" title="Russian presidential election, 1991">
        first Russian presidential elections
       </a>
       , the city authorities arranged for the mayoral elections and a referendum upon the name of the city. The turnout was 65%; 66.13% of the total count of votes went to
       <a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Sobchak" title="Anatoly Sobchak">
        Anatoly Sobchak
       </a>
       , who became the first directly elected
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_Saint_Petersburg_government" title="List of heads of Saint Petersburg government">
        mayor of the city
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Meanwhile, economic conditions started to deteriorate as the country tried to adapt to major changes. For the first time since the 1940s, food
       <a href="/wiki/Rationing" title="Rationing">
        rationing
       </a>
       was introduced, and the city received humanitarian
       <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">
        food aid
       </a>
       from abroad.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orttung_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Orttung-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This dramatic time was depicted in photographic series of Russian photographer
       <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Titarenko" title="Alexey Titarenko">
        Alexey Titarenko
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Economic conditions began to improve only at the beginning of the 21st century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1995 a northern section of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Line_1_of_Saint_Petersburg_Metro" title="Line 1 of Saint Petersburg Metro">
        Kirovsko-Vyborgskaya Line
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Metro" title="Saint Petersburg Metro">
        Saint Petersburg Metro
       </a>
       was cut off by underground flooding, creating a major obstacle to the city development for almost ten years.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1996,
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Anatolyevich_Yakovlev" title="Vladimir Anatolyevich Yakovlev">
        Vladimir Yakovlev
       </a>
       defeated
       <a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Sobchak" title="Anatoly Sobchak">
        Anatoly Sobchak
       </a>
       in the elections for the head of the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_City_Administration" title="Saint Petersburg City Administration">
        city administration
       </a>
       . The title of the city head was changed from "mayor" to "governor". In 2000 Yakovlev won re-election. His second term expired in 2004; the long-awaited restoration of broken subway connection was expected to finish by that time. But in 2003 Yakovlev suddenly resigned, leaving the governor's office to
       <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Matviyenko" title="Valentina Matviyenko">
        Valentina Matviyenko
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG/220px-Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG/330px-Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG/440px-Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ushinskogo_St_Saint_Petersburg_15May2010.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Standard "Home-Ship" (1970s–1980s)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The law on election of the City Governor was changed, breaking the tradition of democratic election by a universal suffrage. In 2006 the
       <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Legislative Assembly of Saint Petersburg">
        city legislature
       </a>
       re-approved Matviyenko as governor. Residential building had intensified again;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_estate_pricing" title="Real estate pricing">
        real-estate prices
       </a>
       inflated greatly, which caused many new problems for the preservation of the historical part of the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although the central part of the city has a
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       designation (there are about 8,000 architectural monuments in Petersburg), the preservation of its historical and architectural environment became controversial.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After 2005, the demolition of older buildings in the historical centre was permitted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2006
       <a href="/wiki/Gazprom" title="Gazprom">
        Gazprom
       </a>
       announced an ambitious project to erect a
       <a href="/wiki/Okhta_Center" title="Okhta Center">
        396-meter skyscraper
       </a>
       opposite to
       <a href="/wiki/Smolny" title="Smolny">
        Smolny
       </a>
       , which
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (April 2013)">
           according to whom?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       could result in the loss of the unique line of Petersburg landscape.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Urgent protests by citizens and prominent public figures of Russia against this project were not considered by Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Matviyenko" title="Valentina Matviyenko">
        Valentina Matviyenko
       </a>
       and the city authorities until December 2010, when after the statement of President
       <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">
        Dmitry Medvedev
       </a>
       , the city decided to find a more appropriate location for this project. In the same year, the new location for the project was relocated to
       <a href="/wiki/Lakhta,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Lakhta, Saint Petersburg">
        Lakhta
       </a>
       , a historical area northwest of the center city, and the new project would be named
       <a href="/wiki/Lakhta_Center" title="Lakhta Center">
        Lakhta Center
       </a>
       . Construction was approved by Gazprom and the city administration and commenced in 2012. The Lakhta Center would be the first
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Russia" title="List of tallest buildings in Russia">
        tallest skyscraper in Russia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Europe" title="List of tallest buildings in Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       that is outside of
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">
        Moscow
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="noprint">
       <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="">
         <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_Saint_Petersburg_from_Palace_Bridge.jpg" title="The Neva River flows through much of the centre of the city.
