          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_Saint_Petersburg_from_Palace_Bridge.jpg" title="File:Panorama of Saint Petersburg from Palace Bridge.jpg">
           </a>
          </div>
          The
          <a href="/wiki/Neva_River" title="Neva River">
           Neva River
          </a>
          flows through much of the centre of the city. Left – the
          <a href="/wiki/Old_Saint_Petersburg_Stock_Exchange_and_Rostral_Columns" title="Old Saint Petersburg Stock Exchange and Rostral Columns">
           Spit of Vasilievsky Island
          </a>
          , center –
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Neva" title="River Neva">
           River Neva
          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Fortress" title="Peter and Paul Fortress">
           Peter and Paul Fortress
          </a>
          and
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinity_Bridge_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Trinity Bridge (Saint Petersburg)">
           Trinity Bridge
          </a>
          , right –
          <a href="/wiki/Palace_Embankment" title="Palace Embankment">
           Palace Embankment
          </a>
          with the
          <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">
           Winter Palace
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
        Main article:
        <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Geography of Saint Petersburg">
         Geography of Saint Petersburg
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
         <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spb-locator.svg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="3437" data-file-width="3579" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Spb-locator.svg/220px-Spb-locator.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Spb-locator.svg/330px-Spb-locator.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Spb-locator.svg/440px-Spb-locator.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
           Territory of the federal subject of Saint Petersburg
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Petersburg_30.36553E_59.94613N.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1932" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Saint_Petersburg_30.36553E_59.94613N.jpg/220px-Saint_Petersburg_30.36553E_59.94613N.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Saint_Petersburg_30.36553E_59.94613N.jpg/330px-Saint_Petersburg_30.36553E_59.94613N.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Saint_Petersburg_30.36553E_59.94613N.jpg/440px-Saint_Petersburg_30.36553E_59.94613N.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
           Satellite image of Saint Petersburg
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The area of Saint Petersburg city proper is 605.8 square kilometers (233.9 sq mi). The area of the federal subject is 1,439 square kilometers (556 sq mi), which contains Saint Petersburg proper (consisting of eighty-one municipal
       <a href="/wiki/Okrug" title="Okrug">
        okrugs
       </a>
       ), nine municipal towns – (
       <a href="/wiki/Kolpino" title="Kolpino">
        Kolpino
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Krasnoye_Selo" title="Krasnoye Selo">
        Krasnoye Selo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">
        Kronstadt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lomonosov,_Russia" title="Lomonosov, Russia">
        Lomonosov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pavlovsk,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Pavlovsk, Saint Petersburg">
        Pavlovsk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Petergof" title="Petergof">
        Petergof
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pushkin_(town)" title="Pushkin (town)">
        Pushkin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sestroretsk" title="Sestroretsk">
        Sestroretsk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zelenogorsk,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Zelenogorsk, Saint Petersburg">
        Zelenogorsk
       </a>
       ) – and twenty-one municipal settlements.
      </p>
      <p>
       Petersburg is situated on the middle
       <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">
        taiga
       </a>
       lowlands along the shores of the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_Bay" title="Neva Bay">
        Neva Bay
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">
        Gulf of Finland
       </a>
       , and islands of the river delta. The largest are
       <a href="/wiki/Vasilyevsky_Island" title="Vasilyevsky Island">
        Vasilyevsky Island
       </a>
       (besides the
       <a href="/wiki/Artificial_island" title="Artificial island">
        artificial island
       </a>
       between Obvodny canal and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fontanka" title="Fontanka">
        Fontanka
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Kotlin_Island" title="Kotlin Island">
        Kotlin
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_Bay" title="Neva Bay">
        Neva Bay
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Petrogradsky_Island" title="Petrogradsky Island">
        Petrogradsky
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dekabristov_Island" title="Dekabristov Island">
        Dekabristov
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Krestovsky_Island" title="Krestovsky Island">
        Krestovsky
       </a>
       . The latter together with
       <a href="/wiki/Yelagin_Island" title="Yelagin Island">
        Yelagin
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kamenny_Island" title="Kamenny Island">
        Kamenny Island
       </a>
       are covered mostly by parks. The
       <a href="/wiki/Karelian_Isthmus" title="Karelian Isthmus">
        Karelian Isthmus
       </a>
       , North of the city, is a popular
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tourist_destination" title="Tourist destination">
        resort area
       </a>
       . In the south Saint Petersburg crosses the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Klint" title="Baltic Klint">
        Baltic-Ladoga Klint
       </a>
       and meets the
       <a href="/wiki/Izhora_Plateau" title="Izhora Plateau">
        Izhora Plateau
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The elevation of Saint Petersburg ranges from the sea level to its highest point of 175.9 meters (577 ft) at the Orekhovaya Hill in the
       <a href="/wiki/Duderhof_Heights" title="Duderhof Heights">
        Duderhof Heights
       </a>
       in the south. Part of the city's territory west of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liteyny_Prospekt" title="Liteyny Prospekt">
        Liteyny Prospekt
       </a>
       is no higher than 4 meters (13 ft)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
        above sea level
       </a>
       , and has suffered from numerous floods.
       <a href="/wiki/Floods_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Floods in Saint Petersburg">
        Floods in Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       are triggered by a long wave in the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       , caused by meteorological conditions, winds and shallowness of the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_Bay" title="Neva Bay">
        Neva Bay
       </a>
       . The four most disastrous floods occurred in 1824 (421 centimeters or 166 inches above sea level, during which over three hundred buildings were destroyed
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ), 1924 (380 centimeters or 150 inches), 1777 (321 centimeters or 126 inches), 1955 (293 centimeters or 115 inches), and 1975 (281 centimeters or 111 inches). To prevent floods, the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Dam" title="Saint Petersburg Dam">
        Saint Petersburg Dam
       </a>
       has been constructed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the 18th century the terrain in the city has been raised artificially, at some places by more than 4 meters (13 ft), making mergers of several islands, and changing the hydrology of the city. Besides the Neva and its tributaries, other important rivers of the federal subject of Saint Petersburg are
       <a href="/wiki/Sestra_River_(Leningrad_Oblast)" title="Sestra River (Leningrad Oblast)">
        Sestra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Okhta_River_(Neva_basin)" title="Okhta River (Neva basin)">
        Okhta
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Izhora_River" title="Izhora River">
        Izhora
       </a>
       . The largest lake is Sestroretsky Razliv in the north, followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Lakhtinsky_Razliv" title="Lakhtinsky Razliv">
        Lakhtinsky Razliv
       </a>
       , Suzdal Lakes and other smaller lakes.
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to location at ca. 60° N
       <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">
        latitude
       </a>
       the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Day_length" title="Day length">
        day length
       </a>
       in Petersburg varies across seasons, ranging from 5 hours 53 minutes to 18 hours 50 minutes. A period from mid-May to mid-July when twilight may last all night is called
       <i>
        the
        <a href="/wiki/Midnight_sun" title="Midnight sun">
         white nights
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Climate of Saint Petersburg">
        Climate of Saint Petersburg
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Under the
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       , Saint Petersburg is classified as
       <i>
        Dfb
       </i>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">
        humid continental climate
       </a>
       . Distinct moderating influence of the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       cyclones result in warm, humid and short summers and long, moderately cold wet winters. Climate of Saint Petersburg is close to the climate of
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       , although colder in winter and warmer in summer because of its more eastern location.
      </p>
      <p>
       The average maximum temperature in July is 23 °C (73 °F), and the average minimum temperature in February is −8.5 °C (16.7 °F); an extreme temperature of 37.1 °C (98.8 °F) occurred during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Northern_Hemisphere_summer_heat_wave" title="2010 Northern Hemisphere summer heat wave">
        2010 Northern Hemisphere summer heat wave
       </a>
       . A winter minimum of −35.9 °C (−32.6 °F) was recorded in 1883. The average annual temperature is 5.8 °C (42.4 °F). The Neva River within the city limits usually freezes up in November–December and break-up occurs in April. From December to March there are 118 days average with snow cover, which reaches an average snow depth of 19 cm (7.5 in) by February.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pogoda_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pogoda-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The frost-free period in the city lasts on average for about 135 days. Despite St. Petersburg's northern location, its winters are warmer than Moscow's due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">
        Gulf of Finland
       </a>
       and some
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">
        Gulf Stream
       </a>
       influence from Scandinavian winds that can bring temperature slightly above freezing. The city also has a slightly warmer climate than its suburbs. Weather conditions are quite variable all year round.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="noprint">
       <p>
        Average annual
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">
         precipitation
        </a>
        varies across the city, averaging 660 millimeters (26 in) per year and reaching maximum in late summer. Soil moisture is almost always high because of lower
        <a href="/wiki/Evapotranspiration" title="Evapotranspiration">
         evapotranspiration
        </a>
        due to the cool climate.
        <a href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" title="Relative humidity">
         Air humidity
        </a>
        is 78% on average, and there is on average, 165
        <a href="/wiki/Overcast" title="Overcast">
         overcast
        </a>
        days per year.
       </p>

      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">
        Toponymy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Toponymy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (September 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The first and fairly rich chapter of the history of the local
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/toponym" title="wiktionary:toponym">
        toponymy
       </a>
       is the story of the own name of the city itself. The
       <a href="/wiki/Name_day" title="Name day">
        name day
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">
        Peter I
       </a>
       falls on June 29, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">
        Russian Orthodox Church
       </a>
       observes the memory of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">
        Saint
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apostle_(Christian)" title="Apostle (Christian)">
        Apostles
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">
        Peter
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">
        Paul
       </a>
       . The consecration of the small wooden church in their names (its construction began simultaneously with the citadel) made them the heavenly patrons of the
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Fortress" title="Peter and Paul Fortress">
        Peter and Paul Fortress
       </a>
       , while St. Peter at the same time became the
       <a href="/wiki/Eponym" title="Eponym">
        eponym
       </a>
       of the whole city. In June 1703
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">
        Peter the Great
       </a>
       officially gave the site the name
       <i>
        Sankt Pieter Burkh
       </i>
       (an emulation of
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       topografical suffix
       <i>
        -burg
       </i>
       , which refers to fortified towns and places, as Peter was a
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Neerlandophile
       </a>
       ) which was subsequently
       <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">
        russefied
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="894" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg/170px-Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg/255px-Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg/340px-Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peter_der-Grosse_1838.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         While not originally named for Tsar
         <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">
          Peter the Great
         </a>
         , during World War I the city was changed from the Germanic "Peterburg" to "Petrograd" in his honour
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A 14- to 15-letter-long name, composed of the three
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Word_root" title="Word root">
        roots
       </a>
       proved too cumbersome, and a lot of shortened versions appeared in habitual use. The first General Governor of the city
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Danilovich_Menshikov" title="Aleksandr Danilovich Menshikov">
        Menshikov
       </a>
       is maybe also the author of the first nickname of Petersburg which he called
       <i>
        Петри
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Petri
       </i>
       ). It took some years until the known Russian spelling of this name finally settled. In 1740s
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">
        Mikhail Lomonosov
       </a>
       uses a derivative of
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
        Greek
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="el">
        Πετρόπολις
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        Petropolis
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Петрополис
       </i>
       ) in a russified form
       <i>
        Petropol
        <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">
         '
        </span>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Петрополь
       </i>
       ). A combo
       <i>
        Piterpol
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Питерпол
       </i>
       ) also appears at this time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nester_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nester-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In any case, eventually the usage of prefix "
       <i>
        Sankt-
       </i>
       " ceased except for the formal official documents, where a three-letter abbreviation "СПб" (
       <i>
        SPb
       </i>
       ) was very widely used as well.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1830s
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">
        Alexander Pushkin
       </a>
       translated the "foreign" city name of "Saint Petersburg" to the more Russian
       <i>
        Petrograd
       </i>
       in one of his poems. However, it was only on 31 [
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">
        O.S.
       </a>
       18 August] 1914, after
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        the war
       </a>
       with Germany had begun, that tsar
       <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">
        Nicholas II
       </a>
       renamed the capital to Petrograd. Since the prefix 'Saint' was omitted,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       this act also changed the
       <a href="/wiki/Eponym" title="Eponym">
        eponym
       </a>
       and the "patron" of the city, from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apostle_Peter" title="Apostle Peter">
        Apostle Peter
       </a>
       to Peter the Great,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       its founder.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="451" data-file-width="674" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg/220px-St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg/330px-St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg/440px-St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St_Petersburg_port_entrance_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         From 1924 to 1991 the city was known as 'Leningrad'. This is a picture of the Saint Petersburg port entrance with an old 'Ленинград' (Leningrad) sign
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the
       <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">
        October Revolution
       </a>
       the name
       <i>
        Red Petrograd
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Красный Петроград
       </i>
       ) was often used in newspapers and other prints until the city was renamed
       <i>
        Leningrad
       </i>
       in January 1924.
      </p>
      <p>
       A referendum on reversing the renaming of
       <i>
        Leningrad
       </i>
       was held on June 12, 1991, with 54.86% of voters (with a turnout of 65%) supporting "
       <i>
        Saint Petersburg
       </i>
       ". Renaming the city
       <i>
        Petrograd
       </i>
       was not an option. This change officially took effect on September 6, 1991.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orttung_32-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Orttung-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Meanwhile, the oblast whose administrative center is also in Saint Petersburg is still named
       <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast" title="Leningrad Oblast">
        Leningrad
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Having passed the role of capital to Petersburg, Moscow never relinquished the title of "capital", being called
       <i>
        pervoprestolnaya
       </i>
       ("first-throned") for 200 years. An equivalent name for Petersburg, the "Northern Capital", has re-entered usage today since several federal institutions were recently moved from Moscow to Saint Petersburg. Solemn descriptive names like "the city of three revolutions" and "the cradle of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/October_revolution" title="October revolution">
        October revolution
       </a>
       " used in Soviet era are reminders of the pivotal events in national history that occurred here. For their part, poetic names of the city, like the "
       <a href="/wiki/Venice_of_the_North" title="Venice of the North">
        Venice of the North
       </a>
       " and the "Northern
       <a href="/wiki/Palmyra" title="Palmyra">
        Palmyra
       </a>
       " emphasize town-planning and architectural features contrasting these parallels to the northern location of this
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalopolis_(city_type)" title="Megalopolis (city type)">
        megalopolis
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Petropolis
       </i>
       is a translation of a city name to Greek, and is also a kind of descriptive name:
       <a class="extiw" href="https://el.wikipedia.org/wiki/%CE%A0%CE%AD%CF%84%CF%81%CF%89%CE%BC%CE%B1" title="el:Πέτρωμα">
        Πέτρ~
       </a>
       is a Greek root for "stone", so the "city from stone" emphasizes the material that had been forcibly made obligatory for construction from the very first years of the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nester_45-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nester-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (Its official Greek name is
       <i>
        Αγία Πετρούπολη
       </i>
       .)
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Demographics of Saint Petersburg">
        Demographics of Saint Petersburg
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dundicha.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2851" data-file-width="3752" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Dundicha.JPG/220px-Dundicha.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Dundicha.JPG/330px-Dundicha.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Dundicha.JPG/440px-Dundicha.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dundicha.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Soviet era apartment buildings in Saint Petersburg, July 2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82))).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3672" data-file-width="4896" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82%29%29%29.jpg/220px-%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82%29%29%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82%29%29%29.jpg/330px-%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82%29%29%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82%29%29%29.jpg/440px-%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82%29%29%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%98%D0%B4%D1%91%D0%BC_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8E%D1%82))).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Metro" title="Saint Petersburg Metro">
          Saint Petersburg Metro
         </a>
         passengers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is the second largest city in Russia. As of the 2017 Rosstat, the federal subject's population is 5,281,579 or 3.6% of the total population of Russia;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2017Rosstat_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-2017Rosstat-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       up from 4,879,566 (3.4%) recorded in the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Census_(2010)" title="Russian Census (2010)">
        2010 Census
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Census_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010Census-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and up from 5,023,506 recorded in the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Census_(1989)" title="Soviet Census (1989)">
        1989 Census
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1989Census_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-1989Census-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Vital statistics for 2016
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Births: 72 879 (13.9 per 1000)
       </li>
       <li>
        Deaths: 61 459 (11.7 per 1000)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
         <a href="#cite_note-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Total fertility rate:
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
         <a href="#cite_note-51">
          [51]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       2009 – 1.34 | 2010 – 1.38 | 2011 – 1.38 | 2012 – 1.48 | 2013 – 1.48 | 2014 – 1.52 | 2015 – 1.59 | 2016 – 1.65(e)
      </p>
      <p>
       The 2010 Census recorded the ethnic composition as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Census_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010Census-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Russian 80.1%,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Russia" title="Ukrainians in Russia">
        Ukrainian
       </a>
       1.3%,
       <a href="/wiki/Belarusians_in_Russia" title="Belarusians in Russia">
        Belarusians
       </a>
       0.8%,
       <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">
        Tatar
       </a>
       0.6%,
       <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Russia" title="Armenians in Russia">
        Armenian
       </a>
       0.6%, Jewish 0.5%,
       <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">
        Uzbek
       </a>
       0.4%,
       <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">
        Tajik
       </a>
       0.3%,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azeris_in_Russia" title="Azeris in Russia">
        Azeri
       </a>
       0.3%,
       <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">
        Georgian
       </a>
       0.2%,
       <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">
        Moldovan
       </a>
       0.2%,
       <a href="/wiki/Ingrian_Finns" title="Ingrian Finns">
        Finns
       </a>
       0.1%, other – 1.3%. The ethnicity of the remaining 13.4% of the inhabitants was not specified.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 20th century, the city experienced dramatic population changes. From 2.4 million residents in 1916 its population dropped to less than 740,000 by 1920 during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_(1917)" title="Russian Revolution (1917)">
        Russian Revolution of 1917
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">
        Russian Civil War
       </a>
       . The minorities of Germans, Poles, Finns, Estonians and Latvians were almost completely
       <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">
        transferred
       </a>
       from Leningrad during the 1930s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martin_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-martin-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From 1941 to the end of 1943, population dropped from 3 million to less than 600,000, as people died in battles, starved to death during the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">
        Siege of Leningrad
       </a>
       , or were evacuated. After the siege, some of the evacuees returned, but most influx was due to migration from other parts of the Soviet Union. The city absorbed about 3 million people in the 1950s and grew to over 5 million in the 1980s. From 1991 to 2006 the city's population decreased to 4.6 million, while the suburban population increased due to privatization of land and massive move to suburbs. Based on the 2010 census results the population is over 4.8 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demoscape0163_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Demoscape0163-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">
        birth rate
       </a>
       remained lower than the
       <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">
        death rate
       </a>
       (until the 2012
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gks.ru_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gks.ru-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) ; people over 65 constitute more than twenty percent of the population; and the median age is about 40 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since 2012 the
       <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">
        birth rate
       </a>
       became higher than the
       <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">
        death rate
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gks.ru_55-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-gks.ru-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       People in urban Saint Petersburg lived mostly in apartments. Between 1918 and the 1990s, the Soviets
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">
        nationalised
       </a>
       housing and forced residents to share communal apartments (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kommunal_apartment" title="Kommunal apartment">
         kommunalkas
        </a>
       </i>
       ). With 68% living in shared flats in the 1930s, Leningrad was the city in the USSR with the largest number of
       <i>
        kommunalkas
       </i>
       . Resettling residents of
       <i>
        kommunalkas
       </i>
       is now on the way out, albeit shared apartments are still not uncommon. As new boroughs were built on the outskirts in the 1950s–1980s, over half a million low income families eventually received free apartments, and about an additional hundred thousand condos were purchased. While economic and social activity is concentrated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Saint_Petersburg" title="Central Saint Petersburg">
        historic city centre
       </a>
       , the richest part of Saint Petersburg, most people live in
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">
        commuter areas
       </a>
       . For the first half of 2007, the birth rate was 9.1 per 1000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Politics of Saint Petersburg">
        Politics of Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Administrative divisions of Saint Petersburg">
        Administrative divisions of Saint Petersburg
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="2525" data-file-width="3361" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/%D0%A1%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9.jpg/220px-%D0%A1%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/%D0%A1%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9.jpg/330px-%D0%A1%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/%D0%A1%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9.jpg/440px-%D0%A1%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          The
          <a href="/wiki/Smolny_Institute" title="Smolny Institute">
           Smolny Institute
          </a>
          , seat of the governor
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St_Petersburg,_Mariinskiy_Palace.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="2188" data-file-width="3810" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/St_Petersburg%2C_Mariinskiy_Palace.jpg/220px-St_Petersburg%2C_Mariinskiy_Palace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/St_Petersburg%2C_Mariinskiy_Palace.jpg/330px-St_Petersburg%2C_Mariinskiy_Palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/St_Petersburg%2C_Mariinskiy_Palace.jpg/440px-St_Petersburg%2C_Mariinskiy_Palace.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          The city assembly meets in the
          <a href="/wiki/Mariinsky_Palace" title="Mariinsky Palace">
           Mariinsky Palace
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is a
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">
        federal subject
       </a>
       of Russia (a
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">
        federal city
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The political life of Saint Petersburg is regulated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Charter of Saint Petersburg">
        Charter of Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       adopted by the city legislature in 1998.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The superior executive body is the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_City_Administration" title="Saint Petersburg City Administration">
        Saint Petersburg City Administration
       </a>
       , led by the
       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Governor of Saint Petersburg">
        city governor
       </a>
       (mayor before 1996). Saint Petersburg has a
       <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">
        single-chamber
       </a>
       legislature, the
       <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Legislative Assembly of Saint Petersburg">
        Saint Petersburg Legislative Assembly
       </a>
       , which is the city's
       <a href="/wiki/Regional_parliaments_of_Russia" title="Regional parliaments of Russia">
        regional parliament
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the federal law passed in 2004, heads of federal subjects, including the governor of Saint Petersburg, were nominated by the
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">
        President of Russia
       </a>
       and approved by local legislatures. Should the legislature disapprove the nominee, the President could dissolve it. The former governor,
       <a href="/wiki/Valentina_Matviyenko" title="Valentina Matviyenko">
        Valentina Matviyenko
       </a>
       , was approved according to the new system in December 2006. She was the only woman governor in the whole of Russia until her resignation on August 22, 2011. Matviyenko stood for elections as member of the Regional Council of Saint Petersburg and won comprehensively with allegations of rigging and ballot stuffing by the opposition. Russian President
       <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">
        Dmitry Medvedev
       </a>
       has already backed her for the position of Speaker to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federation_Council_of_Russia" title="Federation Council of Russia">
        Federation Council of the Federal Assembly of the Russian Federation
       </a>
       and her election qualifies her for that job. After her resignation,
       <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Poltavchenko" title="Georgy Poltavchenko">
        Georgy Poltavchenko
       </a>
       was appointed as the new acting governor the same day. In 2012, following passage of a new federal law,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       restoring direct elections of heads of federal subjects, the city charter was again amended to provide for direct elections of governor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg city is divided into
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Administrative divisions of Saint Petersburg">
        eighteen districts
       </a>
       . Saint Petersburg is also the unofficial but
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       administrative centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast" title="Leningrad Oblast">
        Leningrad Oblast
       </a>
       , and of the
       <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Federal_District" title="Northwestern Federal District">
        Northwestern Federal District
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Constitutional Court of the Russian Federation">
        Constitutional Court of Russia
       </a>
       moved to Saint Petersburg from Moscow in May 2008.
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg and Leningrad Oblast, being two different federal subjects, share a number of local departments of federal executive agencies and courts, such as court of arbitration, police,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service_(Russia)" title="Federal Security Service (Russia)">
        FSB
       </a>
       , postal service, drug enforcement administration, penitentiary service, federal registration service, and other federal services.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Economy of Saint Petersburg">
        Economy of Saint Petersburg
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg/220px-Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg/330px-Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg/440px-Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Admiralty_Shipyard.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Shipyard" title="Admiralty Shipyard">
          Admiralty Shipyard
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-10.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg_International_Economic_Forum" title="St. Petersburg International Economic Forum">
          Saint Petersburg International Economic Forum
         </a>
         is a major Russian investment forum hosted by Mohd Yazid Arshad
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2098" data-file-width="3200" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg/220px-Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg/330px-Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg/440px-Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Power_Machines_building_SPB.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Power Machines plant building on Sverdlovskaya embankment in Saint Petersburg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is a major trade gateway, serving as the financial and industrial centre of Russia, with specializations in oil and gas trade; shipbuilding yards;
       <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">
        aerospace industry
       </a>
       ; technology, including radio, electronics, software, and computers; machine building, heavy machinery and transport, including tanks and other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_technology_and_equipment" title="Military technology and equipment">
        military equipment
       </a>
       ; mining;
       <a href="/wiki/Tool" title="Tool">
        instrument
       </a>
       manufacture; ferrous and nonferrous
       <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">
        metallurgy
       </a>
       (production of aluminium alloys); chemicals,
       <a href="/wiki/Drug" title="Drug">
        pharmaceuticals
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Medical_equipment" title="Medical equipment">
        medical equipment
       </a>
       ; publishing and printing; food and catering; wholesale and retail; textile and
       <a href="/wiki/Clothing" title="Clothing">
        apparel
       </a>
       industries; and many other businesses. It was also home to
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lessner&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lessner (page does not exist)">
        Lessner
       </a>
       , one of Russia's two pioneering automobile manufacturers (along with
       <a href="/wiki/Russo-Balt" title="Russo-Balt">
        Russo-Baltic
       </a>
       ); it was founded by machine tool and boiler maker G. A. Lessner in 1904, with designs by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Boris_Loutsky&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Boris Loutsky (page does not exist)">
        Boris Loutsky
       </a>
       , and it survived until 1910.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Ten percent of the world's power
       <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">
        turbines
       </a>
       are made there at the
       <a href="/wiki/Leningradsky_Metallichesky_Zavod" title="Leningradsky Metallichesky Zavod">
        LMZ
       </a>
       , which built over two thousand turbines for
       <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">
        power plants
       </a>
       across the world. Major local industries are
       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_Shipyard" title="Admiralty Shipyard">
        Admiralty Shipyard
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Shipyard" title="Baltic Shipyard">
        Baltic Shipyard
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/LOMO" title="LOMO">
        LOMO
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kirov_Plant" title="Kirov Plant">
        Kirov Plant
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elektrosila" title="Elektrosila">
        Elektrosila
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Izhorskiye_Zavody" title="Izhorskiye Zavody">
        Izhorskiye Zavody
       </a>
       ; also registered in Saint Petersburg are
       <a href="/wiki/Sovcomflot" title="Sovcomflot">
        Sovkomflot
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Petersburg_Fuel_Company" title="Petersburg Fuel Company">
        Petersburg Fuel Company
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=SIBUR&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="SIBUR (page does not exist)">
        SIBUR
       </a>
       among other major Russian and international companies.
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg has three large cargo
       <a href="/wiki/Ports_of_the_Baltic_Sea" title="Ports of the Baltic Sea">
        seaports
       </a>
       : Bolshoi Port Saint Petersburg,
       <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">
        Kronstadt
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Lomonosov,_Russia" title="Lomonosov, Russia">
        Lomonosov
       </a>
       . International
       <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">
        cruise liners
       </a>
       have been served at the passenger port at
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Morskoy_Vokzal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Morskoy Vokzal (page does not exist)">
        Morskoy Vokzal
       </a>
       on the south-west of
       <a href="/wiki/Vasilyevsky_Island" title="Vasilyevsky Island">
        Vasilyevsky Island
       </a>
       . In 2008 the first two berths were opened at the
       <a href="/wiki/Passenger_Port_of_St._Petersburg" title="Passenger Port of St. Petersburg">
        New Passenger Port
       </a>
       on the west of the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The new port is part of the city's "Marine Facade" development project
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is due to have seven berths in operation by 2010.
      </p>
      <p>
       A complex system of riverports on both banks of the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_River" title="Neva River">
        Neva River
       </a>
       are interconnected with the system of seaports, thus making Saint Petersburg the main link between the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       and the rest of Russia through the
       <a href="/wiki/Volga%E2%80%93Baltic_Waterway" title="Volga–Baltic Waterway">
        Volga-Baltic Waterway
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Mint" title="Saint Petersburg Mint">
        Saint Petersburg Mint
       </a>
       (Monetny Dvor), founded in 1724, is one of the largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mint_(coin)" title="Mint (coin)">
        mints
       </a>
       in the world, it mints
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">
        Russian coins
       </a>
       , medals and badges. Saint Petersburg is also home to the oldest and largest Russian foundry,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Monumentskulptura&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Monumentskulptura (page does not exist)">
        Monumentskulptura
       </a>
       , which made thousands of sculptures and statues that are now gracing public parks of Saint Petersburg, as well as many other cities. Monuments and
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_sculpture" title="Bronze sculpture">
        bronze statues
       </a>
       of the Tsars, as well as other important historic figures and dignitaries, and other world famous monuments, such as the sculptures by
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Clodt_von_J%C3%BCrgensburg" title="Peter Clodt von Jürgensburg">
        Peter Clodt von Jürgensburg
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Troubetzkoy" title="Paolo Troubetzkoy">
        Paolo Troubetzkoy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antokolsky" title="Mark Antokolsky">
        Mark Antokolsky
       </a>
       , and others, were made there.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2007,
       <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">
        Toyota
       </a>
       opened a
       <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Camry" title="Toyota Camry">
        Camry
       </a>
       plant after investing 5 billion roubles (approx. 200 mln dollars) in Shushary, one of the southern suburbs of Saint Petersburg.
       <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">
        Opel
       </a>
       , Hyundai and Nissan have signed deals with the
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Russia" title="Politics of Russia">
        Russian government
       </a>
       to build their automotive plants in Saint Petersburg too. Automotive and auto-parts industry is on the rise there during the last decade.
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is the location of a significant brewery and distillery industry. It is known as the "beer capital" of Russia, due to the supply and quality of local water, contributing over 30% of the domestic production of beer with its five large-scale breweries including Europe's second largest brewery
       <a href="/wiki/Baltika_Breweries" title="Baltika Breweries">
        Baltika
       </a>
       , Vena (both operated by BBH),
       <a href="/wiki/Heineken_International" title="Heineken International">
        Heineken Brewery
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stenka_Razin" title="Stenka Razin">
        Stepan Razin
       </a>
       (both by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heineken_Pilsener" title="Heineken Pilsener">
        Heineken
       </a>
       ) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tinkoff_brewery" title="Tinkoff brewery">
        Tinkoff brewery
       </a>
       (SUN-
       <a href="/wiki/InBev" title="InBev">
        InBev
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The city has a lot of local
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Distillery" title="Distillery">
        distilleries
       </a>
       that produce a broad range of
       <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">
        vodka
       </a>
       brands. The oldest ones is
       <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9B%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B7" title="ru:Ливиз">
        LIVIZ
       </a>
       (founded in 1897). Among the youngest is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Standard_Vodka" title="Russian Standard Vodka">
        Russian Standard Vodka
       </a>
       introduced in Moscow in 1998, which opened in 2006 a new $60 million distillery in Petersburg (an area of 30,000 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (320,000 sq ft), production rate of 22,500 bottles per hour). In 2007 this brand was exported to over 70 countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg has the second largest
       <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">
        construction industry
       </a>
       in Russia, including commercial, housing and road construction.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2006 Saint Petersburg's city budget was 179.9 billion rubles (about 6.651 billion US$ at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tables_of_historical_exchange_rates_to_the_USD" title="Tables of historical exchange rates to the USD">
        2006 exchange rates
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is planned to double by 2012. The federal subject's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_Regional_Product" title="Gross Regional Product">
        Gross Regional Product
       </a>
       as of 2015
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was 3,24 trillion
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">
        Russian rubles
       </a>
       (about 50 billion US$ at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tables_of_historical_exchange_rates_to_the_USD" title="Tables of historical exchange rates to the USD">
        2015 exchange rates
       </a>
       ), ranked 4th in Russia, after Moscow,
       <a href="/wiki/Tyumen_Oblast" title="Tyumen Oblast">
        Tyumen Oblast
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">
        Moscow Oblast
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or 580,000 rubles per capita (about 9,500 US$ at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tables_of_historical_exchange_rates_to_the_USD" title="Tables of historical exchange rates to the USD">
        2015 exchange rates
       </a>
       ), ranked 12th among Russia's federal subjects,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       contributed mostly by wholesale and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retailing" title="Retailing">
        retail trade
       </a>
       and repair services (24.7%) as well as processing industry (20.9%) and transportation and telecommunications (15.1%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Budget revenues of the city in 2009 amounted to 294.3 billion rubles (about 10.044 billion US$ at 2009 exchange rates), expenses – 336.3 billion rubles (about 11.477 billion US$ at 2009 exchange rates). The budget deficit amounted to about 42 billion rubles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (about 1.433 billion US$ at 2009 exchange rates)
      </p>
      <p>
       By 2015, St. Petersburg takes the 4th place on economy scales among all subjects of the Russian Federation, conceding only to Moscow, the Tyumen and Moscow Region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">
        Cityscape
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">

       <a href="/wiki/Landmarks_of_Saint_Petersburg" title="Landmarks of Saint Petersburg">

       </a>
      </div>

      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

          Smolny Convent
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peter_the_Great_Bridge2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Peter_the_Great_Bridge2.jpg/220px-Peter_the_Great_Bridge2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Peter_the_Great_Bridge2.jpg/330px-Peter_the_Great_Bridge2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Peter_the_Great_Bridge2.jpg/440px-Peter_the_Great_Bridge2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
