          Bolsheokhtinsky Bridge
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Auferstehungskirche_(Sankt_Petersburg).JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3869" data-file-width="3984" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Auferstehungskirche_%28Sankt_Petersburg%29.JPG/220px-Auferstehungskirche_%28Sankt_Petersburg%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Auferstehungskirche_%28Sankt_Petersburg%29.JPG/330px-Auferstehungskirche_%28Sankt_Petersburg%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Auferstehungskirche_%28Sankt_Petersburg%29.JPG/440px-Auferstehungskirche_%28Sankt_Petersburg%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Auferstehungskirche_(Sankt_Petersburg).JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Savior_on_Blood" title="Church of the Savior on Blood">
          Church of the Savior on Blood
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg has three skyscrapers: Leader Tower (140 m), Alexander Nevsky (124 m) and Atlantic City (105 m) all three being situated far away from the historical centre. Regulations forbid construction of tall buildings in the city centre. The 310-meter (1,020 ft) tall
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_TV_Tower" title="Saint Petersburg TV Tower">
        Saint Petersburg TV Tower
       </a>
       is the tallest completed structure in the city. However, there was a controversial project endorsed by the city authorities, and known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Okhta_Center" title="Okhta Center">
        Okhta Center
       </a>
       , to build a 396 meters (1,299 ft)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures_in_the_world" title="List of tallest buildings and structures in the world">
        supertall
       </a>
       skyscraper. In 2008, the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Monuments_Fund" title="World Monuments Fund">
        World Monuments Fund
       </a>
       included the Saint Petersburg historic skyline on the watch list of the 100 most endangered sites due to the expected construction, which threatens to alter it drastically.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Okhta Center project has been finally cancelled at the end of 2010 and instead of that
       <a href="/wiki/Lakhta_Center" title="Lakhta Center">
        Lakhta Center
       </a>
       project is started at the city outskirts. The complex will include 463-metre-tall (1,519-foot) office skyscraper and several low rise mixed use buildings. The Lakhta Center project has caused much less controversy and, unlike the previous unbuilt project, is not seen by
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       as a potential threat to the city's cultural heritage because it is located far away from the historical centre. Skyscraper construction has already started, and the building is set to be completed in 2018. It is assumed that the building will be the tallest in Russia and Europe.
      </p>
      <p>
       Unlike in Moscow, in Saint Petersburg the historic architecture of the city centre, mostly consisting of
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">
        Baroque
       </a>
       and neoclassical buildings of the 18th and 19th centuries, has been largely preserved; although a number of buildings were demolished after the Bolsheviks' seizure of power, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">
        Siege of Leningrad
       </a>
       and in recent years.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The oldest of the remaining building is a wooden house built for
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">
        Peter I
       </a>
       in 1703 on the shore of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neva" title="Neva">
        Neva
       </a>
       near Trinity Square. Since 1991 the
       <a href="/wiki/Historic_Centre_of_Saint_Petersburg_and_Related_Groups_of_Monuments" title="Historic Centre of Saint Petersburg and Related Groups of Monuments">
        Historic Centre of Saint Petersburg and Related Groups of Monuments
       </a>
       in Saint Petersburg and Leningrad Oblast have been listed by
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Site
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The ensemble of
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Fortress" title="Peter and Paul Fortress">
        Peter and Paul Fortress
       </a>
       with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Cathedral" title="Peter and Paul Cathedral">
        Peter and Paul Cathedral
       </a>
       takes a dominant position on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zayachy_Island" title="Zayachy Island">
        Zayachy Island
       </a>
       along the right bank of the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_River" title="Neva River">
        Neva River
       </a>
       . Each noon a cannon fires a blank shot from the fortress. The
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Mosque" title="Saint Petersburg Mosque">
        Saint Petersburg Mosque
       </a>
       , the largest mosque in Europe when opened in 1913, is situated on the right bank nearby. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spit_of_Vasilievsky_Island" title="Spit of Vasilievsky Island">
        Spit of Vasilievsky Island
       </a>
       , which splits the river into two largest armlets, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshaya_Neva" title="Bolshaya Neva">
        Bolshaya Neva
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaya_Neva" title="Malaya Neva">
        Malaya Neva
       </a>
       , is connected to the northern bank (
       <a href="/wiki/Petrogradsky_Island" title="Petrogradsky Island">
        Petrogradsky Island
       </a>
       ) via the
       <a href="/wiki/Exchange_Bridge" title="Exchange Bridge">
        Exchange Bridge
       </a>
       and occupied by the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Saint_Petersburg_Stock_Exchange_and_Rostral_Columns" title="Old Saint Petersburg Stock Exchange and Rostral Columns">
        Old Saint Petersburg Stock Exchange and Rostral Columns
       </a>
       . The southern coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Vasilyevsky_Island" title="Vasilyevsky Island">
        Vasilyevsky Island
       </a>
       along the Bolshaya Neva features some of the city's oldest buildings, dating from the 18th century, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Kunstkamera" title="Kunstkamera">
        Kunstkamera
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Collegia" title="Twelve Collegia">
        Twelve Collegia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Menshikov_Palace" title="Menshikov Palace">
        Menshikov Palace
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Academy_of_Arts" title="Imperial Academy of Arts">
        Imperial Academy of Arts
       </a>
       . It hosts one of two campuses of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University" title="Saint Petersburg State University">
        Saint Petersburg State University
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       On the southern, left bank of the Neva, connected to the spit of Vasilyevsky Island via the
       <a href="/wiki/Palace_Bridge" title="Palace Bridge">
        Palace Bridge
       </a>
       , lie the
       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty_building,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Admiralty building, Saint Petersburg">
        Admiralty building
       </a>
       , the vast
       <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">
        Hermitage Museum
       </a>
       complex stretching along the
       <a href="/wiki/Palace_Embankment" title="Palace Embankment">
        Palace Embankment
       </a>
       , which includes the baroque
       <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">
        Winter Palace
       </a>
       , former official residence of Russian emperors, as well as the neoclassical
       <a href="/wiki/Marble_Palace" title="Marble Palace">
        Marble Palace
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace" title="Winter Palace">
        Winter Palace
       </a>
       faces
       <a href="/wiki/Palace_Square" title="Palace Square">
        Palace Square
       </a>
       , the city's main square with the
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Column" title="Alexander Column">
        Alexander Column
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nevsky_Prospekt" title="Nevsky Prospekt">
        Nevsky Prospekt
       </a>
       , also situated on the left bank of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neva" title="Neva">
        Neva
       </a>
       , is the main avenue in the city. It starts at the
       <a href="/wiki/Admiralty" title="Admiralty">
        Admiralty
       </a>
       and runs eastwards next to
       <a href="/wiki/Palace_Square" title="Palace Square">
        Palace Square
       </a>
       . Nevsky Prospekt crosses the
       <a href="/wiki/Moyka_River" title="Moyka River">
        Moika
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Green_Bridge_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Green Bridge (Saint Petersburg)">
        Green Bridge
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Griboyedov_Canal" title="Griboyedov Canal">
        Griboyedov Canal
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Kazansky_Bridge" title="Kazansky Bridge">
        Kazansky Bridge
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Sadovaya_Street" title="Sadovaya Street">
        Garden Street
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fontanka" title="Fontanka">
        Fontanka
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Anichkov_Bridge" title="Anichkov Bridge">
        Anichkov Bridge
       </a>
       ), meets
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liteyny_Prospekt" title="Liteyny Prospekt">
        Liteyny Prospekt
       </a>
       and proceeds to
       <a href="/wiki/Vosstaniya_Square" title="Vosstaniya Square">
        Uprising Square
       </a>
       near the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskovsky_Rail_Terminal_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Moskovsky Rail Terminal (Saint Petersburg)">
        Moskovsky railway station
       </a>
       , where it meets
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ligovsky_Prospekt" title="Ligovsky Prospekt">
        Ligovsky Prospekt
       </a>
       and turns to the
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Lavra" title="Alexander Nevsky Lavra">
        Alexander Nevsky Lavra
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Passage_(department_store)" title="Passage (department store)">
        The Passage
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_of_St._Catherine_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Catholic Church of St. Catherine (Saint Petersburg)">
        Catholic Church of St. Catherine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Singer_House" title="Singer House">
        Book House
       </a>
       (former
       <a href="/wiki/Singer_Corporation" title="Singer Corporation">
        Singer Manufacturing Company
       </a>
       Building in the
       <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">
        Art Nouveau
       </a>
       style),
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Hotel_Europe" title="Grand Hotel Europe">
        Grand Hotel Europe
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_Church_of_Saint_Peter_and_Saint_Paul" title="Lutheran Church of Saint Peter and Saint Paul">
        Lutheran Church of Saint Peter and Saint Paul
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Gostiny_Dvor" title="Great Gostiny Dvor">
        Great Gostiny Dvor
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Russia" title="National Library of Russia">
        Russian National Library
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexandrinsky_Theatre" title="Alexandrinsky Theatre">
        Alexandrine Theatre
       </a>
       behind
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Mikeshin" title="Mikhail Mikeshin">
        Mikeshin
       </a>
       's statue of
       <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">
        Catherine the Great
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazan_Cathedral,_St._Petersburg" title="Kazan Cathedral, St. Petersburg">
        Kazan Cathedral
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Stroganov_Palace" title="Stroganov Palace">
        Stroganov Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anichkov_Palace" title="Anichkov Palace">
        Anichkov Palace
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Beloselsky-Belozersky_Palace" title="Beloselsky-Belozersky Palace">
        Beloselsky-Belozersky Palace
       </a>
       are all situated along that avenue.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Lavra" title="Alexander Nevsky Lavra">
        Alexander Nevsky Lavra
       </a>
       , intended to house the relics of
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky" title="Alexander Nevsky">
        St. Alexander Nevsky
       </a>
       , is an important centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Religious_studies" title="Religious studies">
        Christian education
       </a>
       in Russia. It also contains the
       <a href="/wiki/Tikhvin_Cemetery" title="Tikhvin Cemetery">
        Tikhvin Cemetery
       </a>
       with graves of many notable Petersburgers.
      </p>
      <p>
       On the territory between the Neva and Nevsky Prospekt the
       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Savior_on_Blood" title="Church of the Savior on Blood">
        Church of the Savior on Blood
       </a>
       , Mikhailovsky Palace housing the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">
        Russian Museum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Field_of_Mars_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Field of Mars (Saint Petersburg)">
        Field of Mars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Michael%27s_Castle" title="Saint Michael's Castle">
        St. Michael's Castle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Summer_Garden" title="Summer Garden">
        Summer Garden
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tauride_Palace" title="Tauride Palace">
        Tauride Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Smolny_Institute" title="Smolny Institute">
        Smolny Institute
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Smolny_Convent" title="Smolny Convent">
        Smolny Convent
       </a>
       are located.
      </p>
      <p>
       Many notable landmarks are situated to the west and south of the Admiralty Building, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Cathedral,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Trinity Cathedral, Saint Petersburg">
        Trinity Cathedral
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mariinsky_Palace" title="Mariinsky Palace">
        Mariinsky Palace
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Astoria_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Hotel Astoria (Saint Petersburg)">
        Hotel Astoria
       </a>
       , famous
       <a href="/wiki/Mariinsky_Theatre" title="Mariinsky Theatre">
        Mariinsky Theatre
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Holland_Island" title="New Holland Island">
        New Holland Island
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Isaac's Cathedral">
        Saint Isaac's Cathedral
       </a>
       , the largest in the city, and
       <a href="/wiki/Senate_Square_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Senate Square (Saint Petersburg)">
        Senate Square
       </a>
       , also known as
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Decembrist%27s_Square&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Decembrist's Square (page does not exist)">
        Decembrist's Square
       </a>
       with the
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Horseman" title="Bronze Horseman">
        Bronze Horseman
       </a>
       , 18th century equestrian monument to
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">
        Peter the Great
       </a>
       , which is considered among the city's most recognisable symbols. Other symbols of Saint Petersburg include the
       <a href="/wiki/Weather_vane" title="Weather vane">
        weather vane
       </a>
       in the shape of a small ship on top of the Admiralty's golden spire and the golden angel on top of the Peter and Paul Cathedral. The Palace Bridge
       <a href="/wiki/Drawbridge" title="Drawbridge">
        drawn
       </a>
       at night is yet another symbol of the city. Every night during the navigation period from April to November, 22 bridges across the Neva and main canals are drawn to let ships pass in and out of the Baltic Sea according to a schedule.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was not until 2004 that the first high bridge across the Neva, which does not need to be drawn,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Obukhovsky_Bridge" title="Big Obukhovsky Bridge">
        Big Obukhovsky Bridge
       </a>
       , was opened. There are hundreds of smaller
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_bridges_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="List of bridges in Saint Petersburg">
        bridges in Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       spanning across numerous canals and distributaries of the Neva, some of the most important of which are the
       <a href="/wiki/Moyka_River" title="Moyka River">
        Moika
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fontanka" title="Fontanka">
        Fontanka
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Griboyedov_Canal" title="Griboyedov Canal">
        Griboyedov Canal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Obvodny_Canal" title="Obvodny Canal">
        Obvodny Canal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Karpovka_River" title="Karpovka River">
        Karpovka
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Smolenka_River" title="Smolenka River">
        Smolenka
       </a>
       . Due to the intricate web of canals, Saint Petersburg is often called
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Venice_of_the_North" title="Venice of the North">
         Venice of the North
        </a>
       </i>
       . The rivers and canals in the city centre are lined with granite embankments. The embankments and bridges are separated from rivers and canals by
       <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">
        granite
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Cast_iron" title="Cast iron">
        cast iron
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Parapet" title="Parapet">
        parapets
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Southern suburbs of the city feature former imperial residences, including
       <a href="/wiki/Petergof" title="Petergof">
        Petergof
       </a>
       , with majestic fountain cascades and parks,
       <a href="/wiki/Tsarskoye_Selo" title="Tsarskoye Selo">
        Tsarskoe Selo
       </a>
       , with the baroque
       <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Palace" title="Catherine Palace">
        Catherine Palace
       </a>
       and the neoclassical
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Palace" title="Alexander Palace">
        Alexander Palace
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Pavlovsk_Palace" title="Pavlovsk Palace">
        Pavlovsk
       </a>
       , which contains a domed palace of
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">
        Emperor Paul
       </a>
       and one of the largest English-style parks in Europe. Some other residences situated nearby and making part of the world heritage site, including a castle and park in
       <a href="/wiki/Gatchina" title="Gatchina">
        Gatchina
       </a>
       , actually belong to
       <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast" title="Leningrad Oblast">
        Leningrad Oblast
       </a>
       rather than Saint Petersburg. Another notable suburb is
       <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">
        Kronstadt
       </a>
       with its 19th-century fortifications and naval monuments, occupying the
       <a href="/wiki/Kotlin_Island" title="Kotlin Island">
        Kotlin Island
       </a>
       in the Gulf of Finland.
      </p>
      <p>
       Since around the end of the 20th century a great deal of active building and restoration works have been carried out in a number of the city's older districts. The authorities have recently been compelled to transfer the ownership of state-owned private residences in the city centre to private lessors. Many older buildings have been reconstructed to allow their use as apartments and penthouses.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of these structures, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Commodity_and_Stock_Exchange" title="Saint Petersburg Commodity and Stock Exchange">
        Saint Petersburg Commodity and Stock Exchange
       </a>
       have been recognised as town-planning errors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1808" data-file-width="2736" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg/220px-Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg/330px-Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg/440px-Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia_-_Bolshoi_Zal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Bolshoi Zal (Grand Hall) of
         <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonia" title="Saint Petersburg Philharmonia">
          Saint Petersburg Philharmonia
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg has a significant historical and cultural heritage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 18th and 19th-century architectural ensemble of the city and its environs is preserved in virtually unchanged form. For various reasons (including large-scale destruction during
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       and construction of modern buildings during the postwar period in the largest historical centers of Europe), Saint Petersburg has become a unique reserve of European architectural styles of the past three centuries. Saint Petersburg's loss of capital city status helped the city to retain many of its pre-revolutionary buildings, as modern architectural 'prestige projects' tended to be built in Moscow; this largely prevented the rise of mid-to-late-20th-century architecture and helped maintain the architectural appearance of the historic city center.
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is inscribed on the
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       World Heritage list as an area with 36 historical architectural complexes and around 4000 outstanding individual monuments of architecture, history and culture. New tourist programs and sightseeing tours have been developed for those wishing to see Saint Petersburg's cultural heritage.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_(26).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_%2826%29.jpg/220px-Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_%2826%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_%2826%29.jpg/330px-Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_%2826%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_%2826%29.jpg/440px-Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_%2826%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ermit%C3%A1%C5%BE_(26).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Small Italian Skylight Room in the
         <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">
          Hermitage Museum
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city has 221 museums, 2000 libraries, more than 80 theaters, 100 concert organizations, 45 galleries and exhibition halls, 62 cinemas and around 80 other cultural establishments. Every year the city hosts around 100 festivals and various competitions of art and culture, including more than 50 international ones.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite the
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Economic history of the Russian Federation">
        economic instability of the 1990s
       </a>
       , not a single major theatre or museum was closed in Saint Petersburg; on the contrary many new ones opened, for example a private museum of puppets (opened in 1999) is the third museum of its kind in Russia, where collections of more than 2000 dolls are presented including 'The multinational Saint Petersburg' and '
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pushkin%27s_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pushkin's Petersburg (page does not exist)">
        Pushkin's Petersburg
       </a>
       '. The museum world of Saint Petersburg is incredibly diverse. The city is not only home to the world-famous
       <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">
        Hermitage Museum
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">
        Russian Museum
       </a>
       with its rich collection of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_art" title="Russian art">
        Russian art
       </a>
       , but also the palaces of Saint Petersburg and its suburbs, so-called small town museums and others like the museum of famous Russian writer
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dostoyevsky" title="Dostoyevsky">
        Dostoyevsky
       </a>
       ;
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Museum_of_Musical_Instruments_(Saint_Petersburg)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Museum of Musical Instruments (Saint Petersburg) (page does not exist)">
        Museum of Musical Instruments
       </a>
       , the museum of decorative arts and the museum of professional orientation.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Russia" title="Music of Russia">
        musical life
       </a>
       of Saint Petersburg is rich and diverse, with the city now playing host to a number of annual carnivals.
      </p>
      <p>
       Ballet performances occupy a special place in the cultural life of Saint Petersburg. The Petersburg School of Ballet is named as one of the best in the world. Traditions of the Russian classical school have been passed down from generation to generation among outstanding educators. The art of famous and prominent Saint Petersburg dancers like
       <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Nureyev" title="Rudolf Nureyev">
        Rudolf Nureyev
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Makarova" title="Natalia Makarova">
        Natalia Makarova
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Baryshnikov" title="Mikhail Baryshnikov">
        Mikhail Baryshnikov
       </a>
       was, and is, admired throughout the world. Contemporary Petersburg ballet is made up not only of traditional Russian classical school, but also ballets by those like
       <a href="/wiki/Boris_Eifman" title="Boris Eifman">
        Boris Eifman
       </a>
       , who expanded the scope of strict classical
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_ballet" title="Russian ballet">
        Russian ballet
       </a>
       to almost unimaginable limits. Remaining faithful to the classical basis (he was a choreographer at the
       <a href="/wiki/Vaganova_Academy_of_Russian_Ballet" title="Vaganova Academy of Russian Ballet">
        Vaganova Academy of Russian Ballet
       </a>
       ), he combined
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_ballet" title="Classical ballet">
        classical ballet
       </a>
       with the
       <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">
        avant-garde style
       </a>
       , and then, in turn, with acrobatics, rhythmic gymnastics, dramatic expressiveness,
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Russia" title="Cinema of Russia">
        cinema
       </a>
       , color, light, and finally with spoken word.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communications">
        Media and communications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Media and communications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       All major Russian newspapers are active in Saint Petersburg. The city has a developed telecommunications system. In 2014
       <a href="/wiki/Rostelecom" title="Rostelecom">
        Rostelecom
       </a>
       , the national operator announced it began a major modernization of the fixed-line network in the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Society_and_culture_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Society and culture in Saint Petersburg">
        Society and culture in Saint Petersburg
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">
        Museums
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Museums">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:908px;">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="">
        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg" title="The State Hermitage Museum (building on the right)">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="1258" data-file-width="4626" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg/900px-Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg/1350px-Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg/1800px-Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg 2x" width="900"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sankt_Petersburg.palatul_de_iarna.N.jpg" title="File:Sankt Petersburg.palatul de iarna.N.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Hermitage_Museum" title="State Hermitage Museum">
          State Hermitage Museum
         </a>
         (building on the right)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is home to more than two hundred museums, many of them hosted in historic buildings. The largest of the museums is the
       <a href="/wiki/Hermitage_Museum" title="Hermitage Museum">
        Hermitage Museum
       </a>
       , featuring interiors of the former imperial residence and a vast collection of art. The
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">
        Russian Museum
       </a>
       is a large museum devoted specifically to Russian fine art. The apartments of some famous Petersburgers, including
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">
        Alexander Pushkin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoyevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoyevsky">
        Fyodor Dostoyevsky
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Rimsky-Korsakov" title="Nikolai Rimsky-Korsakov">
        Nikolai Rimsky-Korsakov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Feodor_Chaliapin" title="Feodor Chaliapin">
        Feodor Chaliapin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Blok" title="Alexander Blok">
        Alexander Blok
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Nabokov" title="Vladimir Nabokov">
        Vladimir Nabokov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anna_Akhmatova" title="Anna Akhmatova">
        Anna Akhmatova
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Zoshchenko" title="Mikhail Zoshchenko">
        Mikhail Zoshchenko
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Brodsky" title="Joseph Brodsky">
        Joseph Brodsky
       </a>
       , as well as some palace and park ensembles of the southern suburbs and notable architectural monuments such as St. Isaac's Cathedral, have also been turned into public museums.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Kunstkamera" title="Kunstkamera">
        Kunstkamera
       </a>
       , with its collection established in 1714 by Peter the Great to collect curiosities from all over the world, is sometimes considered the first museum in Russia, which has evolved into the present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Kunstkamera" title="Kunstkamera">
        Peter the Great Museum of Anthropology and Ethnography
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Ethnography_Museum" title="Russian Ethnography Museum">
        Russian Ethnography Museum
       </a>
       , which has been split from the Russian Museum, is devoted to the cultures of the people of Russia, the
       <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">
        former Soviet Union
       </a>
       and Russian Empire.
      </p>
      <p>
       A number of museums provide insight into the Soviet history of Saint Petersburg, including the Museum of the Blockade, which describes the
       <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">
        Siege of Leningrad
       </a>
       and the Museum of Political History, which explains many authoritarian features of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S.S.R." title="U.S.S.R.">
        U.S.S.R.
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Other notable museums include the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Naval_Museum" title="Central Naval Museum">
        Central Naval Museum
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Zoological_Museum_of_the_Zoological_Institute_of_the_Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Zoological Museum of the Zoological Institute of the Russian Academy of Sciences">
        Zoological Museum
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Central_Soil_Museum_by_V._V._Dokuchaev" title="The Central Soil Museum by V. V. Dokuchaev">
        Central Soil Museum
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Railway_Museum" title="Russian Railway Museum">
        Russian Railway Museum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Suvorov_Museum" title="Suvorov Museum">
        Suvorov Museum
       </a>
       , Museum of the Siege of Leningrad,
       <a href="/wiki/Erarta" title="Erarta">
        Erarta Museum of Contemporary Art
       </a>
       , the largest non-governmental Museum of contemporary art in Russia,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Museum_of_History" title="Saint Petersburg Museum of History">
        Saint Petersburg Museum of History
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_and_Paul_Fortress" title="Peter and Paul Fortress">
        Peter and Paul Fortress
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Military_Historical_Museum_of_Artillery,_Engineers_and_Signal_Corps" title="Military Historical Museum of Artillery, Engineers and Signal Corps">
        Artillery Museum
       </a>
       , which includes not only artillery items, but also a huge collection of other military equipment, uniforms and decorations.
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 267.33333333333px">
        <div style="width: 267.33333333333px">

           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Russian_Museum" title="Russian Museum">
            Russian Museum
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 183.33333333333px">
        <div style="width: 183.33333333333px">
