           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           The
           <a href="/wiki/Kunstkamera" title="Kunstkamera">
            Kunstkamera
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 204px">
        <div style="width: 204px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 202px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="1569" data-file-width="2640" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%D0%92%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg/303px-%D0%92%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%D0%92%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg/455px-%D0%92%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/%D0%92%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg/606px-%D0%92%D1%85%D0%BE%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%B7%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B8.jpg 2x" width="202"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Military_Historical_Museum_of_Artillery,_Engineers_and_Signal_Corps" title="Military Historical Museum of Artillery, Engineers and Signal Corps">
            Military Historical Museum
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 174.66666666667px">
        <div style="width: 174.66666666667px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 172.66666666667px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cruiser_Aurora.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="2084" data-file-width="3000" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cruiser_Aurora.jpg/259px-Cruiser_Aurora.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cruiser_Aurora.jpg/389px-Cruiser_Aurora.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Cruiser_Aurora.jpg/518px-Cruiser_Aurora.jpg 2x" width="173"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Museum_ship" title="Museum ship">
            Museum ship
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Russian_cruiser_Aurora" title="Russian cruiser Aurora">
            cruiser Aurora
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="386" data-file-width="500" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg/220px-Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg/330px-Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg/440px-Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mariinsky_Theatre_in_Saint_Petersburg.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The main auditorium of the Mariinsky Theatre
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Among the city's more than fifty theatres is the world-famous
       <a href="/wiki/Mariinsky_Theatre" title="Mariinsky Theatre">
        Mariinsky Theatre
       </a>
       (also known as the Kirov Theatre in the USSR), home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Mariinsky_Ballet" title="Mariinsky Ballet">
        Mariinsky Ballet
       </a>
       company and opera. Leading ballet dancers, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Vaslav_Nijinsky" title="Vaslav Nijinsky">
        Vaslav Nijinsky
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anna_Pavlova" title="Anna Pavlova">
        Anna Pavlova
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Nureyev" title="Rudolf Nureyev">
        Rudolph Nureyev
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Baryshnikov" title="Mikhail Baryshnikov">
        Mikhail Baryshnikov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Galina_Ulanova" title="Galina Ulanova">
        Galina Ulanova
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Makarova" title="Natalia Makarova">
        Natalia Makarova
       </a>
       , were principal stars of the Mariinsky ballet.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first music school, the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Conservatory" title="Saint Petersburg Conservatory">
        Saint Petersburg Conservatory
       </a>
       , was founded in 1862 by the Russian pianist and composer
       <a href="/wiki/Anton_Rubinstein" title="Anton Rubinstein">
        Anton Rubinstein
       </a>
       . The school alumni have included such notable composers as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyotr_Tchaikovsky" title="Pyotr Tchaikovsky">
        Pyotr Tchaikovsky
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Prokofiev" title="Sergei Prokofiev">
        Sergei Prokofiev
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Artur_Kapp" title="Artur Kapp">
        Artur Kapp
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Tobias" title="Rudolf Tobias">
        Rudolf Tobias
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">
        Dmitri Shostakovich
       </a>
       , who taught at the conservatory during the 1960s, bringing it additional fame. The renowned Russian composer
       <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Rimsky-Korsakov" title="Nikolai Rimsky-Korsakov">
        Nikolai Rimsky-Korsakov
       </a>
       also taught at the conservatory from 1871 to 1905. Among his students were
       <a href="/wiki/Igor_Stravinsky" title="Igor Stravinsky">
        Igor Stravinsky
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Glazounov" title="Alexander Glazounov">
        Alexander Glazounov
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatoly_Liadov" title="Anatoly Liadov">
        Anatoly Liadov
       </a>
       and others. The former St. Petersburg apartment of Rimsky-Korsakov has been faithfully preserved as the
       <a href="/wiki/Rimsky-Korsakov_Apartment_and_Museum" title="Rimsky-Korsakov Apartment and Museum">
        composer's only museum
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shou_alie_parusa.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="641" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Shou_alie_parusa.jpg/220px-Shou_alie_parusa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Shou_alie_parusa.jpg/330px-Shou_alie_parusa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Shou_alie_parusa.jpg/440px-Shou_alie_parusa.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shou_alie_parusa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_Sails_(tradition)" title="Scarlet Sails (tradition)">
          Scarlet Sails
         </a>
         celebration on the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neva" title="Neva">
          Neva
         </a>
         River in Saint Petersburg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Dmitri Shostakovich, who was born and raised in Saint Petersburg, dedicated his
       <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._7_(Shostakovich)" title="Symphony No. 7 (Shostakovich)">
        Seventh Symphony
       </a>
       to the city, calling it the "Leningrad Symphony". He wrote the symphony while based in the city during the siege of Leningrad. It was premiered in Samara in March 1942; a few month later, it received its first
       <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_premi%C3%A8re_of_Shostakovich%27s_Symphony_No._7" title="Leningrad première of Shostakovich's Symphony No. 7">
        performance
       </a>
       in the besieged Leningrad at the Bolshoy Philharmonic Hall under the baton of conductor
       <a href="/wiki/Karl_Eliasberg" title="Karl Eliasberg">
        Karl Eliasberg
       </a>
       . It was heard over the radio and was said to have lifted the spirits of the surviving population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1992, the 7th Symphony was performed by the 14 surviving orchestral players of the Leningrad premiere in the same hall as half a century before.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Saint Petersburg Philharmonic Orchestra">
        Leningrad Philharmonic Orchestra
       </a>
       remained one of the best known
       <a href="/wiki/Orchestra" title="Orchestra">
        symphony orchestras
       </a>
       in the world under the leadership of conductors
       <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Mravinsky" title="Yevgeny Mravinsky">
        Yevgeny Mravinsky
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Temirkanov" title="Yuri Temirkanov">
        Yuri Temirkanov
       </a>
       . Mravinsky's term as artistic director of the Leningrad Philharmonic – a term that is possibly the longest of any conductor with any orchestra in modern times – led the orchestra from being a little-known provincial ensemble to it becoming one of the world's most highly regarded orchestras today, especially for the performance of Russian music.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Imperial Choral Capella was founded and modeled after the royal courts of other European capitals.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2255" data-file-width="3400" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg/220px-Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg/330px-Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg/440px-Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alexandrinsky_Theatre.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexandrinsky_Theater" title="Alexandrinsky Theater">
          Alexander theatre
         </a>
         , Saint Petersburg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg has been home to the newest movements in
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">
        popular music
       </a>
       in the country. The first
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       band in the Soviet Union was founded here by
       <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Utyosov" title="Leonid Utyosov">
        Leonid Utyosov
       </a>
       in the 1920s, under the patronage of
       <a href="/wiki/Isaak_Dunayevsky" title="Isaak Dunayevsky">
        Isaak Dunayevsky
       </a>
       . The first jazz club in the Soviet Union was founded here in the 1950s and was later named
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz_club" title="Jazz club">
        jazz club
       </a>
       Kvadrat. In 1956 the popular ensemble
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Druzhba_(band)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Druzhba (band) (page does not exist)">
        Druzhba
       </a>
       was founded by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aleksandr_Bronevitsky&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aleksandr Bronevitsky (page does not exist)">
        Aleksandr Bronevitsky
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Edita_Piekha" title="Edita Piekha">
        Edita Piekha
       </a>
       to become the first popular band in the USSR during the 1950s. In the 1960s student rock-groups
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Argonavty&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Argonavty (page does not exist)">
        Argonavty
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kochevniki&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kochevniki (page does not exist)">
        Kochevniki
       </a>
       and others pioneered a series of unofficial and
       <a href="/wiki/Underground_music" title="Underground music">
        underground rock
       </a>
       concerts and festivals. In 1972
       <a href="/wiki/Boris_Grebenshchikov" title="Boris Grebenshchikov">
        Boris Grebenshchikov
       </a>
       founded the band
       <a href="/wiki/Aquarium_(band)" title="Aquarium (band)">
        Aquarium
       </a>
       , which later grew to huge popularity. Since then "Peter's rock"
       <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">
        music style
       </a>
       was formed.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1970s many bands came out from 'underground' and eventually founded the
       <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Rock_Club" title="Leningrad Rock Club">
        Leningrad Rock Club
       </a>
       , which provided a stage to such bands as
       <a href="/wiki/DDT_(band)" title="DDT (band)">
        DDT
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kino_(band)" title="Kino (band)">
        Kino
       </a>
       , headed by the legendary
       <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Tsoi" title="Viktor Tsoi">
        Viktor Tsoi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alisa" title="Alisa">
        Alisa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zemlyane" title="Zemlyane">
        Zemlyane
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zoopark" title="Zoopark">
        Zoopark
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Piknik" title="Piknik">
        Piknik
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secret_(Russian_band)" title="Secret (Russian band)">
        Secret
       </a>
       and many other popular groups. The first Russian-style happening show
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Mekhanika&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pop Mekhanika (page does not exist)">
        Pop Mekhanika
       </a>
       , mixing over 300 people and animals on stage, was directed by the multi-talented
       <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Kuryokhin" title="Sergey Kuryokhin">
        Sergey Kuryokhin
       </a>
       in the 1980s. The annual International Music Festival SKIF (
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sergey_Kuriokhin_International_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sergey Kuriokhin International Festival (page does not exist)">
        Sergey Kuriokhin International Festival
       </a>
       ) is named after him. In 2004 the
       <a href="/wiki/Kuryokhin_Center" title="Kuryokhin Center">
        Kuryokhin Center
       </a>
       was founded, were the SKIF as well as the Electro-Mechanica festival and Ethnomechanica festival takes place. SKIF focuses on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Experimental_pop_music" title="Experimental pop music">
        experimental pop music
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avant_garde_music" title="Avant garde music">
        avant garde music
       </a>
       , Electro-Mechanica on
       <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">
        electronic music
       </a>
       and Ethnomechanica on
       <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">
        world music
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Today's Saint Petersburg boasts many notable musicians of various genres, from popular Leningrad's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergei_Shnurov" title="Sergei Shnurov">
        Sergei Shnurov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tequilajazzz" title="Tequilajazzz">
        Tequilajazzz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Splean" title="Splean">
        Splean
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Korol_i_Shut" title="Korol i Shut">
        Korol i Shut
       </a>
       , to rock veterans
       <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Shevchuk" title="Yuri Shevchuk">
        Yuri Shevchuk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vyacheslav_Butusov" title="Vyacheslav Butusov">
        Vyacheslav Butusov
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Boyarsky" title="Mikhail Boyarsky">
        Mikhail Boyarsky
       </a>
       . In the early 2000s on a wave of popularity of
       <a href="/wiki/Metalcore" title="Metalcore">
        metalcore
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapcore" title="Rapcore">
        rapcore
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emocore" title="Emocore">
        emocore
       </a>
       and there are such groups as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amatory_(band)" title="Amatory (band)">
        Amatory
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kirpichi" title="Kirpichi">
        Kirpichi
       </a>
       , Psychea,
       <a href="/wiki/Stigmata_(Russian_band)" title="Stigmata (Russian band)">
        Stigmata
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grenouer" title="Grenouer">
        Grenouer
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Animal_Jazz" title="Animal Jazz">
        Animal Jazz
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/White_Nights_Festival" title="White Nights Festival">
        White Nights Festival
       </a>
       in Saint Petersburg is famous for spectacular fireworks and a massive show celebrating the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Academic_term" title="Academic term">
        school year
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Film">
        Film
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Film">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="524" data-file-width="848" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg/220px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg/330px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg/440px-%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD_%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Khabensky" title="Konstantin Khabensky">
          Konstantin Khabensky
         </a>
         , known for his roles in
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Night_Watch_(2004_film)" title="Night Watch (2004 film)">
           Night Watch
          </a>
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Day_Watch_(film)" title="Day Watch (film)">
           Day Watch
          </a>
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/The_Admiral_(2008_film)" title="The Admiral (2008 film)">
           Admiral
          </a>
         </i>
         , is a native of Saint Petersburg.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Over 250 international and Russian movies were filmed in Saint Petersburg.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Well over a thousand feature films about tsars, revolution, people and stories set in Saint Petersburg have been produced worldwide but not filmed in the city. The first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movie_studio" title="Movie studio">
        film studios
       </a>
       were founded in Saint Petersburg in the 20th century and since the 1920s
       <a href="/wiki/Lenfilm" title="Lenfilm">
        Lenfilm
       </a>
       has been the largest film studio based in Saint Petersburg. The first foreign feature movie filmed entirely in Saint Petersburg was the 1997 production of Tolstoy's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Anna_Karenina_(1997_film)" title="Anna Karenina (1997 film)">
         Anna Karenina
        </a>
       </i>
       , starring
       <a href="/wiki/Sophie_Marceau" title="Sophie Marceau">
        Sophie Marceau
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sean_Bean" title="Sean Bean">
        Sean Bean
       </a>
       and made by an international team of British, American, French and Russian filmmakers.
      </p>
      <p>
       The cult comedy
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Irony_of_Fate" title="The Irony of Fate">
         Irony of Fate
        </a>
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (also Ирония судьбы, или С лёгким паром!) is set in Saint Petersburg and pokes fun at Soviet city planning. The 1985 film
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/White_Nights_(1985_film)" title="White Nights (1985 film)">
         White Nights
        </a>
       </i>
       received considerable Western attention for having captured genuine Leningrad street scenes at a time when filming in the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       by Western production companies was generally unheard of. Other movies include
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/GoldenEye" title="GoldenEye">
         GoldenEye
        </a>
       </i>
       (1995),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Midnight_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Midnight in Saint Petersburg">
         Midnight in Saint Petersburg
        </a>
       </i>
       (1996),
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Brother_(1997_film)" title="Brother (1997 film)">
         Brother
        </a>
       </i>
       (1997) and
       <a href="/wiki/Tamil_cinema" title="Tamil cinema">
        Tamil
       </a>
       romantic
       <a href="/wiki/Thriller_(genre)" title="Thriller (genre)">
        thriller film
       </a>
       -
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Dhaam_Dhoom" title="Dhaam Dhoom">
         Dhaam Dhoom
        </a>
       </i>
       (2008).
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Onegin#Film" title="Eugene Onegin">
         Onegin
        </a>
       </i>
       (1999) is based on the
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">
        Pushkin
       </a>
       poem and showcases many
       <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attraction" title="Tourist attraction">
        tourist attractions
       </a>
       . In addition, the Russian romantic comedy,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Piter_FM" title="Piter FM">
         Piter FM
        </a>
       </i>
       , intricately showcases the cityscape, almost as if it were a main character in the film.
      </p>
      <p>
       Several international film festivals are held annually, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Festival_of_Festivals,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Festival of Festivals, Saint Petersburg">
        Festival of Festivals, Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       , as well as the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Message_to_Man_International_Documentary_Film_Festival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Message to Man International Documentary Film Festival (page does not exist)">
        Message to Man International Documentary Film Festival
       </a>
       , since its inauguration in 1988 during the White Nights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Message_To_Man_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Message_To_Man-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment,_4.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2458" data-file-width="3277" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment%2C_4.JPG/220px-St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment%2C_4.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment%2C_4.JPG/330px-St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment%2C_4.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment%2C_4.JPG/440px-St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment%2C_4.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St._Petersburg._Makarova_Embankment,_4.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Pushkin_House" title="Pushkin House">
          Pushkin House
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg has a longstanding and world famous tradition in literature.
       <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoyevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoyevsky">
        Dostoyevsky
       </a>
       called it "The most abstract and intentional city in the world", emphasizing its artificiality, but it was also a symbol of modern disorder in a changing Russia. It frequently appeared to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_language_writers" title="List of Russian language writers">
        Russian writers
       </a>
       as a menacing and inhuman mechanism. The grotesque and often nightmarish image of the city is featured in Pushkin's last poems, the Petersburg stories of
       <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Gogol" title="Nikolai Gogol">
        Gogol
       </a>
       , the novels of
       <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoyevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoyevsky">
        Dostoyevsky
       </a>
       , the verse of
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Blok" title="Alexander Blok">
        Alexander Blok
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Osip_Mandelstam" title="Osip Mandelstam">
        Osip Mandelshtam
       </a>
       , and in the symbolist novel
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Petersburg_(novel)" title="Petersburg (novel)">
         Petersburg
        </a>
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Bely" title="Andrei Bely">
        Andrey Bely
       </a>
       . According to Lotman in his chapter, 'The Symbolism of Saint Petersburg' in
       <i>
        Universe and the Mind
       </i>
       , these writers were inspired by symbolism from within the city itself. The effect of life in Saint Petersburg on the plight of the poor clerk in a society obsessed with hierarchy and status also became an important theme for authors such as
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">
        Pushkin
       </a>
       , Gogol and Dostoyevsky. Another important feature of early Saint Petersburg literature is its mythical element, which incorporates
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_legend" title="Urban legend">
        urban legends
       </a>
       and popular
       <a href="/wiki/Ghost_story" title="Ghost story">
        ghost stories
       </a>
       , as the stories of Pushkin and Gogol included ghosts returning to Saint Petersburg to haunt other characters as well as other fantastical elements, creating a surreal and abstract image of Saint Petersburg.
      </p>
      <p>
       20th-century writers from Saint Petersburg, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Nabokov" title="Vladimir Nabokov">
        Vladimir Nabokov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ayn_Rand" title="Ayn Rand">
        Ayn Rand
       </a>
       , Andrey Bely and
       <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Zamyatin" title="Yevgeny Zamyatin">
        Yevgeny Zamyatin
       </a>
       , along with his apprentices, The
       <a href="/wiki/Serapion_Brothers" title="Serapion Brothers">
        Serapion Brothers
       </a>
       created entire new styles in literature and contributed new insights to the understanding of society through their experience in this city.
       <a href="/wiki/Anna_Akhmatova" title="Anna Akhmatova">
        Anna Akhmatova
       </a>
       became an important leader for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_language_poets" title="List of Russian language poets">
        Russian poetry
       </a>
       . Her poem
       <i>
        Requiem
       </i>
       adumbrates the perils encountered during the Stalinist era. Another notable 20th-century writer from Saint Petersburg is
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Brodsky" title="Joseph Brodsky">
        Joseph Brodsky
       </a>
       , recipient of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">
        Nobel Prize in Literature
       </a>
       (1987). While living in the United States, his writings in English reflected on life in Saint Petersburg from the unique perspective of being both an insider and an outsider to the city in essays such as, "A Guide to a Renamed City" and the nostalgic "In a Room and a Half".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="3041" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg/220px-VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg/330px-VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg/440px-VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VO_Universitet_12_Kollegiy_02-03-2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University" title="Saint Petersburg State University">
          Saint Petersburg State University
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Polytechnical_Institute.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="194" data-file-width="450" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/Polytechnical_Institute.jpg" width="450"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Polytechnic_University" title="Saint Petersburg Polytechnic University">
          Saint Petersburg Polytechnic University
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="646" data-file-width="998" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg/220px-Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg/330px-Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg/440px-Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pulkovo_observatory_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Observatory" title="Pulkovo Observatory">
          Pulkovo Observatory
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Russia" title="Education in Russia">
        Education in Russia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_higher_education_and_academic_institutions_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="List of higher education and academic institutions in Saint Petersburg">
        List of higher education and academic institutions in Saint Petersburg
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       As of 2006
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       /2007 there were 1024 kindergartens, 716
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" title="Public school (government funded)">
        public schools
       </a>
       and 80
       <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">
        vocational
       </a>
       schools in Saint Petersburg.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The largest of the public higher education institutions is
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University" title="Saint Petersburg State University">
        Saint Petersburg State University
       </a>
       , enrolling approximately 32,000 undergraduate students; and the largest non-governmental higher education institutions is the
       <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg_Institute_of_International_Trade,_Economics_and_Law" title="St. Petersburg Institute of International Trade, Economics and Law">
        Institute of International Economic Relations, Economics, and Law
       </a>
       . Other famous universities are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Polytechnic_University" title="Saint Petersburg Polytechnic University">
        Saint Petersburg Polytechnic University
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Herzen_University" title="Herzen University">
        Herzen University
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University_of_Economics_and_Finance" title="Saint Petersburg State University of Economics and Finance">
        Saint Petersburg State University of Economics and Finance
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_engineering-technical_university" title="Military engineering-technical university">
        Saint Petersburg Military engineering-technical university
       </a>
       . However, the public universities are all federal property and do not belong to the city.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Sport in Saint Petersburg">
        Sport in Saint Petersburg
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4792" data-file-width="7188" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg/220px-RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg/330px-RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg/440px-RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RUS-2016-Aerial-SPB-Krestovsky_Stadium_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Krestovsky_Stadium" title="Krestovsky Stadium">
          Krestovsky Stadium
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Leningrad hosted part of the association football tournament during the 1980
       <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">
        Summer Olympics
       </a>
       . The 1994
       <a href="/wiki/Goodwill_Games" title="Goodwill Games">
        Goodwill Games
       </a>
       were also held here.
      </p>
      <p>
       In boating, the first competition here was the 1703
       <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">
        rowing
       </a>
       event initiated by Peter the Great, after the victory over the
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Navy" title="Swedish Navy">
        Swedish fleet
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Yachting" title="Yachting">
        Yachting
       </a>
       events were held by the Russian Navy since the foundation of the city.
       <a href="/wiki/Yacht_club" title="Yacht club">
        Yacht clubs
       </a>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg_River_Yacht_Club" title="St. Petersburg River Yacht Club">
        St. Petersburg River Yacht Club
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_Yacht_Club" title="Neva Yacht Club">
        Neva Yacht Club
       </a>
       , the latter is the oldest yacht club in the world. In the winter, when the sea and lake surfaces are frozen and yachts and dinghies cannot be used, local people sail
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_boat" title="Ice boat">
        ice boats
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">
        Equestrianism
       </a>
       has been a long tradition, popular among the Tsars and aristocracy, as well as part of
       <a href="/wiki/Military_education_and_training" title="Military education and training">
        military training
       </a>
       . Several historic sports arenas were built for equestrianism since the 18th century, to maintain training all year round, such as the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Winter_Stadium_in_Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Winter Stadium in Saint Petersburg (page does not exist)">
        Zimny Stadion
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Konnogvardeisky_Manezh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Konnogvardeisky Manezh (page does not exist)">
        Konnogvardeisky Manezh
       </a>
       , among others.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">
        Chess
       </a>
       tradition was highlighted by the 1914 international tournament, partially funded by the Tsar, in which the title "Grandmaster" was first formally conferred by
       <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">
        Russian Tsar Nicholas II
       </a>
       to five players:
       <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Lasker" title="Emanuel Lasker">
        Lasker
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ra%C3%BAl_Capablanca" title="José Raúl Capablanca">
        Capablanca
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Alekhine" title="Alexander Alekhine">
        Alekhine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Siegbert_Tarrasch" title="Siegbert Tarrasch">
        Tarrasch
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Marshall_(chess_player)" title="Frank Marshall (chess player)">
        Marshall
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SKA_SPb_Logo.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="298" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/SKA_SPb_Logo.png/220px-SKA_SPb_Logo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/38/SKA_SPb_Logo.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SKA_SPb_Logo.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/SKA_Saint_Petersburg" title="SKA Saint Petersburg">
          SKA Saint Petersburg
         </a>
         logo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Kirov_Stadium" title="Kirov Stadium">
        Kirov Stadium
       </a>
       (now demolished) was one of the largest stadiums in the world and home to
       <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">
        FC Zenit Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       from 1950 to 1993 and again in 1995. In 1951 a crowd of 110,000 set the single-game attendance record for Soviet football. In 1984, 2007, 2010 and 2011/2012 Zenit were the champions of the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Top_League" title="Soviet Top League">
        Soviet
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Premier_League" title="Russian Premier League">
        Russian
       </a>
       leagues, respectively, and won the Russian Cup in 1999 and 2010, the
       <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Cup" title="2007–08 UEFA Cup">
        UEFA Cup 2007–08 season
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/2008_UEFA_Super_Cup" title="2008 UEFA Super Cup">
        2008 UEFA Super Cup
       </a>
       . The team leader was local player
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrei_Arshavin" title="Andrei Arshavin">
        Andrei Arshavin
       </a>
       . Zenit play their home games at
       <a href="/wiki/Petrovsky_Stadium" title="Petrovsky Stadium">
        Petrovsky Stadium
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zenit_Stadium" title="New Zenit Stadium">
        New Zenit Stadium
       </a>
       , which will host
       <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">
        2018 FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       matches, is under construction.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also a second professional football club in Saint Petersburg,
       <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Dynamo Saint Petersburg">
        FC Dynamo Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       , which is owned by the historic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dynamo_sports_society" title="Dynamo sports society">
        Dynamo sports society
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Hockey teams in the city include
       <a href="/wiki/SKA_Saint_Petersburg" title="SKA Saint Petersburg">
        SKA Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KHL" title="KHL">
        KHL
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HC_VMF_St._Petersburg" title="HC VMF St. Petersburg">
        HC VMF St. Petersburg
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VHL" title="VHL">
        VHL
       </a>
       , and junior clubs
       <a href="/wiki/SKA-1946" title="SKA-1946">
        SKA-1946
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silver_Lions" title="Silver Lions">
        Silver Lions
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Major_League" title="Russian Major League">
        Russian Major League
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/SKA_Saint_Petersburg" title="SKA Saint Petersburg">
        SKA Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       is one of the most popular in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KHL" title="KHL">
        KHL
       </a>
       , consistently being at or near the top of the league in attendance. Along with their popularity, they are one of the best teams in the KHL right now, as they have won the
       <a href="/wiki/Gagarin_Cup" title="Gagarin Cup">
        Gagarin Cup
       </a>
       twice.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Well-known players on the team include
       <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Datsyuk" title="Pavel Datsyuk">
        Pavel Datsyuk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Kovalchuk" title="Ilya Kovalchuk">
        Ilya Kovalchuk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Gusev" title="Nikita Gusev">
        Nikita Gusev
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Shirokov" title="Sergei Shirokov">
        Sergei Shirokov
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viktor_Tikhonov_(ice_hockey_b._1988)" title="Viktor Tikhonov (ice hockey b. 1988)">
        Viktor Tikhonov
       </a>
       . During the NHL lockout, stars
       <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Kovalchuk" title="Ilya Kovalchuk">
        Ilya Kovalchuk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bobrovsky" title="Sergei Bobrovsky">
        Sergei Bobrovsky
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Tarasenko" title="Vladimir Tarasenko">
        Vladimir Tarasenko
       </a>
       also played for the team. They play their home games at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ice_Palace_Saint_Petersburg" title="Ice Palace Saint Petersburg">
        Ice Palace Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city's long-time basketball team is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BC_Kondrashin_Belov" title="BC Kondrashin Belov">
        BC Kondrashin Belov
       </a>
       , which launched the career of
       <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Kirilenko" title="Andrei Kirilenko">
        Andrei Kirilenko
       </a>
       . Kondrashin Belov won two championships in the
       <a href="/wiki/USSR_Premier_Basketball_League" title="USSR Premier Basketball League">
        USSR Premier League
       </a>
       (1975 and 1992), two
       <a href="/wiki/USSR_Basketball_Cup" title="USSR Basketball Cup">
        USSR Cups
       </a>
       (1978 and 1987), and a
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Basketball_Cup" title="Russian Basketball Cup">
        Russian Cup
       </a>
       title (2011). They also won the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saporta_Cup" title="Saporta Cup">
        Saporta Cup
       </a>
       twice (1973 and 1975). Legends of the club include
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Belov" title="Alexander Belov">
        Alexander Belov
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Kondrashin" title="Vladimir Kondrashin">
        Vladimir Kondrashin
       </a>
       . The city also has a new basketball team,
       <a href="/wiki/B.C._Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="B.C. Zenit Saint Petersburg">
        BC Zenit Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2669" data-file-width="4271" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg/220px-Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg/330px-Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg/440px-Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spb_06-2017_img46_ZSD_bridge_at_Krestovsky_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A section of the
         <a href="/wiki/Western_Rapid_Diameter" title="Western Rapid Diameter">
          Western High-Speed Diameter
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is a major transport hub. The first Russian railway was built here in 1837, and since then the city's transport infrastructure has continued to develop and keep pace with the growth of the city. Petersburg has an extensive system of local roads and railway services, maintains a large public transport system that includes the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tramways_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Tramways in Saint Petersburg">
        Saint Petersburg tram
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Metro" title="Saint Petersburg Metro">
        Saint Petersburg Metro
       </a>
       , and is home to a number of riverine services that convey passengers around the city efficiently and in relative comfort.
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is connected to the rest of Russia and the wider world by a number of federal highways and national and international rail routes.
       <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">
        Pulkovo Airport
       </a>
       serves the majority of air passengers departing from or arriving to the city.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads_and_public_transport">
        Roads and public transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Roads and public transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trolleybus_BKM-321_on_Nevsky_Avenue_(img2).jpg">

        </a>

         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Obvodny_Kanal_(Saint_Petersburg_Metro)" title="Obvodny Kanal (Saint Petersburg Metro)">
          Obvodny Kanal
         </a>
         station, opened in 2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TramMoskovskiyeVorotaSquare2008-04-12-1103c_cut.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1847" data-file-width="2200" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/TramMoskovskiyeVorotaSquare2008-04-12-1103c_cut.jpg/220px-TramMoskovskiyeVorotaSquare2008-04-12-1103c_cut.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/TramMoskovskiyeVorotaSquare2008-04-12-1103c_cut.jpg/330px-TramMoskovskiyeVorotaSquare2008-04-12-1103c_cut.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/TramMoskovskiyeVorotaSquare2008-04-12-1103c_cut.jpg/440px-TramMoskovskiyeVorotaSquare2008-04-12-1103c_cut.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

         Tram on
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Gate_Square" title="Moscow Gate Square">
          Moscow Gate Square
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg/220px-St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg/330px-St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg/440px-St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:St._Petersburg_Russia_Hydrofoil_boat.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Hydrofoil" title="Hydrofoil">
          Hydrofoil
         </a>
         docking in St.Petersburg upon arrival from
         <a href="/wiki/Peterhof_Palace" title="Peterhof Palace">
          Peterhof Palace
         </a>
         (2008).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg has an extensive city-funded network of public transport (buses,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tramways_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Tramways in Saint Petersburg">
        trams
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
        trolleybuses
       </a>
       ) and several hundred routes served by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Marshrutka" title="Marshrutka">
         marshrutkas
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tramways_in_Saint_Petersburg" title="Tramways in Saint Petersburg">
        Trams in Saint Petersburg
       </a>
       used to be the main mean of transport; in the 1980s this was the largest tram network in the world, but many tracks were dismantled in the 2000s.
      </p>
      <p>
       Buses carry up to three million passengers daily, serving over 250 urban and a number of suburban bus routes.
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Metro" title="Saint Petersburg Metro">
        Saint Petersburg Metro
       </a>
       underground rapid transit system was opened in 1955; it now has 5 lines with 67 stations, connecting all five railway terminals, and carrying 2.3 million passengers daily.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Metro stations are often elaborately decorated with materials such as marble and bronze.
      </p>
      <div class="noprint">
       <center>
        <table class="collapsible collapsed" style="border:1px solid #ddd; float:center; margin:5px 5px 0 0;">
         <tr>
          <th style="background:#f5f5f5; padding:5px;">
           <span style="margin:0 10px 0 20px;">
            Saint Petersburg Metro map
           </span>
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td>
           <div class="center">
            <div class="floatnone">
             <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Petersburg_metro_map_ENG.png">
              <img alt="Saint Petersburg metro map ENG.png" data-file-height="3030" data-file-width="2304" height="789" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Saint_Petersburg_metro_map_ENG.png/600px-Saint_Petersburg_metro_map_ENG.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Saint_Petersburg_metro_map_ENG.png/900px-Saint_Petersburg_metro_map_ENG.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Saint_Petersburg_metro_map_ENG.png/1200px-Saint_Petersburg_metro_map_ENG.png 2x" width="600"/>
             </a>
            </div>
           </div>
          </td>
         </tr>
        </table>
       </center>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">
        Traffic jams
       </a>
       are common in the city due to daily commuter traffic volumes, intercity traffic and excessive winter snow. The construction of
       <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highway" title="Controlled-access highway">
        freeways
       </a>
       such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Ring_Road" title="Saint Petersburg Ring Road">
        Saint Petersburg Ring Road
       </a>
       , completed in 2011, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Rapid_Diameter" title="Western Rapid Diameter">
        Western High-Speed Diameter
       </a>
       , completed in 2017, helped partially reduce the traffic in the city. The controversial
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow%E2%80%93Saint_Petersburg_motorway" title="Moscow–Saint Petersburg motorway">
        M11
       </a>
       , also known as the Moscow-Saint Petersburg Motorway, would connect Saint Petersburg and Moscow by a freeway and is expected to be completed before the
       <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">
        Russia FIFA World Cup 2018
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Construction has started in 2010 and the first sections of the freeway was finished in 2014 and 2015.
      </p>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is an important
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_corridor" title="Transport corridor">
        transport corridor
       </a>
       linking
       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">
        Scandinavia
       </a>
       to Russia and Eastern Europe. The city is a node of the
       <a href="/wiki/International_E-road_network" title="International E-road network">
        international European routes
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/European_route_E18" title="European route E18">
        E18
       </a>
       towards
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/European_route_E20" title="European route E20">
        E20
       </a>
       towards
       <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">
        Tallinn
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/European_route_E95" title="European route E95">
        E95
       </a>
       towards
       <a href="/wiki/Pskov" title="Pskov">
        Pskov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">
        Kiev
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">
        Odessa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/European_route_E105" title="European route E105">
        E105
       </a>
       towards
       <a href="/wiki/Petrozavodsk" title="Petrozavodsk">
        Petrozavodsk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Murmansk" title="Murmansk">
        Murmansk
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kirkenes" title="Kirkenes">
        Kirkenes
       </a>
       (north) and towards Moscow and
       <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv" title="Kharkiv">
        Kharkiv
       </a>
       (south).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_Petersburg_public_transportation_statistics">
        Saint Petersburg public transportation statistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Saint Petersburg public transportation statistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Saint Petersburg, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 69 min. 19.6% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 11 min, while 16.1% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 7 km, while 15.% travel for over 12 km in a single direction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Waterways">
        Waterways
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Waterways">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The city is also served by passenger and cargo seaports in the
       <a href="/wiki/Neva_Bay" title="Neva Bay">
        Neva Bay
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">
        Gulf of Finland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       , the river port higher up the Neva and tens of smaller passenger stations on both banks of the Neva river. It is a terminus of both the
       <a href="/wiki/Volga%E2%80%93Baltic_Waterway" title="Volga–Baltic Waterway">
        Volga-Baltic
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Sea_%E2%80%93_Baltic_Canal" title="White Sea – Baltic Canal">
        White Sea-Baltic
       </a>
       waterways.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first high bridge that does not need to be drawn, a 2,824-meter (9,265 ft) long
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Obukhovsky_Bridge" title="Big Obukhovsky Bridge">
        Big Obukhovsky Bridge
       </a>
       , opened in 2004. Meteor
       <a href="/wiki/Hydrofoil" title="Hydrofoil">
        hydrofoils
       </a>
       link the city centre to the coastal towns of
       <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt" title="Kronstadt">
        Kronstadt
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lomonosov,_Russia" title="Lomonosov, Russia">
        Lomonosov
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Petergof" title="Petergof">
        Petergof
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sestroretsk" title="Sestroretsk">
        Sestroretsk
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zelenogorsk,_Saint_Petersburg" title="Zelenogorsk, Saint Petersburg">
        Zelenogorsk
       </a>
       from May through October. In the warmer months many smaller boats and water-taxis maneuver the canals throughout the city.
      </p>
      <p>
       The shipping company
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Peter_Line" title="St Peter Line">
        St Peter Line
       </a>
       operates two ferries that sail from
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       to St Petersburg and from
       <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">
        Stockholm
       </a>
       to St Petersburg.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Russia" title="Rail transport in Russia">
        Rail transport in Russia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="487" data-file-width="732" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/220px-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/330px-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg/440px-%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BF%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD_%D0%B2_%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Sapsan" title="Sapsan">
          Sapsan
         </a>
         high-speed train runs between Moscow and Saint Petersburg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The city is the final destination for a web of intercity and suburban railways, served by five different railway terminals (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltiysky_Rail_Terminal" title="Baltiysky Rail Terminal">
        Baltiysky
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finlyandsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Finlyandsky Rail Terminal">
        Finlyandsky
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ladozhsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Ladozhsky Rail Terminal">
        Ladozhsky
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moskovsky_Rail_Terminal_(Saint_Petersburg)" title="Moskovsky Rail Terminal (Saint Petersburg)">
        Moskovsky
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vitebsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Vitebsky Rail Terminal">
        Vitebsky
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as dozens of non-terminal
       <a href="/wiki/Train_station" title="Train station">
        railway stations
       </a>
       within the federal subject. Saint Petersburg has international railway connections to
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       , Finland, Berlin, Germany and many former republics of the USSR. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riihim%C3%A4ki_%E2%80%93_Saint_Petersburg_Railway" title="Riihimäki – Saint Petersburg Railway">
        Helsinki railway
       </a>
       , which was built in 1870 and is 443 kilometers (275 mi) long, has trains running four times a day, in a journey lasting about three and a half hours with the new
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karelian_Trains_Class_Sm6" title="Karelian Trains Class Sm6">
        Allegro
       </a>
       train.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_%E2%80%93_Saint_Petersburg_Railway" title="Moscow – Saint Petersburg Railway">
        Moscow – Saint Petersburg Railway
       </a>
       opened in 1851, and is 651 kilometers (405 mi) long; the commute to Moscow now requires from three and a half to nine hours.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2009
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Railways" title="Russian Railways">
        Russian Railways
       </a>
       launched a high speed service for the Moscow – Saint Petersburg route. The new train, known as
       <a href="/wiki/Sapsan" title="Sapsan">
        Sapsan
       </a>
       , is a derivative of the popular
       <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro" title="Siemens Velaro">
        Siemens Velaro
       </a>
       train; various versions of this already operate in some European countries. It set records for the fastest train in Russia on May 2, 2009, travelling at 281 km/h (174.6 mph)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and on May 7, 2009, traveling at 290 kilometers per hour (180 mph).
      </p>
      <p>
       Since December 12, 2010
       <a href="/wiki/Karelian_Trains" title="Karelian Trains">
        Karelian Trains
       </a>
       , a joint venture between
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Railways" title="Russian Railways">
        Russian Railways
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VR_Group" title="VR Group">
        VR (Finnish Railways)
       </a>
       , has been running
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karelian_Trains_Class_Sm6" title="Karelian Trains Class Sm6">
        Alstom Pendolino
       </a>
       operated high-speed services between Saint Petersburg's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finlyandsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Finlyandsky Rail Terminal">
        Finlyandsky
       </a>
       and Helsinki's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helsinki_Central_railway_station" title="Helsinki Central railway station">
        Central
       </a>
       railway stations. These services are branded as "Allegro" trains. "Allegro" is known for suffering some big technical problems from time to time, which sometimes result in significant delays and even cancel of tourists' trips.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="noprint">
