      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">
        Air
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Air">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:427px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1379" data-file-width="7424" height="79" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg/425px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg/638px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg/850px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg 2x" width="425"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0_%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%8F.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">
          Pulkovo International Airport
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is served by
       <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">
        Pulkovo International Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and also by three smaller commercial and cargo airports in the suburbs.
       <a href="/wiki/Lappeenranta_Airport" title="Lappeenranta Airport">
        Lappeenranta Airport
       </a>
       , which is located near Saint Petersburg but on the Finnish side of the border is also popular among Russian travellers.
      </p>
      <p>
       Pulkovo airport was opened to passengers as a small aerodrome in 1931. As of 2013
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the Pulkovo airport, which handles over 12 million passengers annually, is the 3rd busiest in Russia after Moscow's
       <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">
        Sheremetyevo
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domodedovo_International_Airport" title="Domodedovo International Airport">
        Domodedovo
       </a>
       . As a result, the steadily increasing passenger traffic has triggered a massive modernization of the entire airport infrastructure. A newly built Terminal 1 of the Pulkovo airport was put into operation on December 4, 2013 and integrated international flights of the former terminal Pulkovo-2. The renovated terminal Pulkovo-1 has been opened for domestic flights as an extension of the Terminal 1 in 2015.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a regular rapid-bus connection (buses 39, 39E, K39) between Pulkovo airport and the
       <a href="/wiki/Moskovskaya_(Saint_Petersburg_Metro)" title="Moskovskaya (Saint Petersburg Metro)">
        Moskovskaya metro station
       </a>
       as well as 24/7 taxi service.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">
        Parks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Parks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Saint Petersburg is home to numerous parks and gardens, some of the most famous of which are situated in the southern suburbs, including one of the largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_garden" title="English garden">
        English gardens
       </a>
       in Europe in
       <a href="/wiki/Pavlovsk_Palace" title="Pavlovsk Palace">
        Pavlovsk
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Sosnovka" title="Sosnovka">
        Sosnovka
       </a>
       is the largest park within the limits of the city proper, occupying 240 ha. The
       <a href="/wiki/Summer_Garden" title="Summer Garden">
        Summer Garden
       </a>
       is the oldest one, dating back to the early 18th century and designed in the regular style. It is situated on the southern bank of the Neva at the head of the Fontanka and is famous for its cast iron railing and marble sculptures.
      </p>
      <p>
       Among other notable parks are the
       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Victory_Park" title="Maritime Victory Park">
        Maritime Victory Park
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Krestovsky_Island" title="Krestovsky Island">
        Krestovsky Island
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow_Victory_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Moscow Victory Park (page does not exist)">
        Moscow Victory Park
       </a>
       in the south, both commemorating the victory over
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">
        Second World War
       </a>
       , as well as the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Central_Park_of_Culture_and_Leisur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Central Park of Culture and Leisur (page does not exist)">
        Central Park of Culture and Leisure
       </a>
       occupying
       <a href="/wiki/Yelagin_Island" title="Yelagin Island">
        Yelagin Island
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tauride_Garden&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tauride Garden (page does not exist)">
        Tauride Garden
       </a>
       around the
       <a href="/wiki/Tauride_Palace" title="Tauride Palace">
        Tauride Palace
       </a>
       . The most common trees grown in the parks are the
       <a href="/wiki/Quercus_robur" title="Quercus robur">
        English oak
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Acer_platanoides" title="Acer platanoides">
        Norway maple
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fraxinus_pennsylvanica" title="Fraxinus pennsylvanica">
        green ash
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Betula_pendula" title="Betula pendula">
        silver birch
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_Larch" title="Siberian Larch">
        Siberian Larch
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picea_pungens" title="Picea pungens">
        blue spruce
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salix_fragilis" title="Salix fragilis">
        crack willow
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tilia" title="Tilia">
        limes
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Populus" title="Populus">
        poplars
       </a>
       . Important
       <a href="/wiki/Xylotheque" title="Xylotheque">
        dendrological collections
       </a>
       dating back to the 19th century are hosted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_Botanical_Garden" title="Saint Petersburg Botanical Garden">
        Saint Petersburg Botanical Garden
       </a>
       and the Park of the Forestry Academy.
      </p>
      <p>
       In order to commemorate 300 years anniversary of Saint Petersburg a new park was laid out. The park is situated in the north western part of the city. The construction was started in 1995. It is planned to connect the park with the pedestrian bridge to the territory of
       <a href="/wiki/Lakhta_Center" title="Lakhta Center">
        Lakhta Center
       </a>
       's recreation areas. In the park 300 trees of valuable sorts, 300 decorative apple-trees, 70 limes. 300 other trees and bushes were planted. These trees were presented to Saint Petersburg by non-commercial and educational organizations of the city, its sister-cities, city of Helsinki, heads of other regions of Russia, German Savings Bank and other people and organizations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Krikalev" title="Sergei Krikalev">
            Sergei Krikalev
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">
        Crime
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Petersburg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Crime">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Russia" title="Crime in Russia">
        Crime in Russia
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tambov_gang" title="Tambov gang">
        Tambov gang
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:508px;">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="">
        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kresty_Prison.jpg" title="The Kresty Prison">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="9400" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kresty_Prison.jpg/500px-Kresty_Prison.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kresty_Prison.jpg/750px-Kresty_Prison.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kresty_Prison.jpg/1000px-Kresty_Prison.jpg 2x" width="500"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kresty_Prison.jpg" title="File:Kresty Prison.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Kresty_Prison" title="Kresty Prison">
          Kresty Prison
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The crime dynamic in Saint Petersburg is tightly associated with the general social situation in the country. A sharp spike in the crime level occurred in the late 1980s/early 1990s as a result of the
       <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">
        Perestroika
       </a>
       -time turmoils (redistribution of property, privatization, decline of living standards, decrease of the effectiveness of
       <a href="/wiki/Militsiya" title="Militsiya">
        militsiya
       </a>
       etc.) By then the city had fallen under the control of a number of organized criminal groups such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tambov_Gang" title="Tambov Gang">
        Tambov Gang
       </a>
       , Malyshev Gang,
       <a href="/wiki/Kazan_phenomenon" title="Kazan phenomenon">
        Kazan Gang
       </a>
       and ethnic criminal groups, engaged in
       <a href="/wiki/Racket_(crime)" title="Racket (crime)">
        racket
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Extortion" title="Extortion">
        extortion
       </a>
       , paying off local government and violent clashes with each other.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the assassinations of City Property Committee chairman and vice-Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Manevich" title="Mikhail Manevich">
        Mikhail Manevich
       </a>
       (1997),
       <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">
        State Duma
       </a>
       deputy
       <a href="/wiki/Galina_Starovoytova" title="Galina Starovoytova">
        Galina Starovoytova
       </a>
       (1998), acting City Legislature Speaker
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Viktor_Novosyolov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Viktor Novosyolov (page does not exist)">
        Viktor Novosyolov
       </a>
       (1999) and a number of prominent businesspeople, Saint Petersburg was dubbed
       <i>
        Capital of Crime
       </i>
       in the Russian press.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There were a number of movies filmed in Saint Petersburg about the life of crime,
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Banditskiy_Peterburg:_Advocat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Banditskiy Peterburg: Advocat (page does not exist)">
         Banditskiy Peterburg: Advocat
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Brother_(1997_film)" title="Brother (1997 film)">
         Brother
        </a>
       </i>
       , reinforcing its image as the Crime Capital of Russia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to official sources the number of crimes committed by foreigners in Saint Petersburg in 2010 increased by 11.1%. Law enforcement authorities consider this was associated with an increased number of people from some
       <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">
        CIS republics
       </a>
       who live in Saint Petersburg illegally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bare_url_110-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bare_url-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the other hand, some media reported that in recent years there had been a notable increase in racially motivated violence, in particular towards
       <a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">
        foreign students
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Racist_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Racist-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One of the notable
       <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">
        white supremacist
       </a>
       groups,
       <i>
        Belaya Energia
       </i>
       (White Energy, inspired by US "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Power" title="White Power">
        White Power
       </a>
       " groups) has reportedly been one of the gangs involved in murdering foreign university students.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Racist_111-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Racist-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The official portal of the Government of Saint Petersburg provided data on significant improvements in the crime situation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bare_url_110-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bare_url-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In particular, it was reported that the number of crimes against tourists had decreased by more than half during 2009–2011.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2012, Canada's Department of Foreign Affairs warned LGBT travellers about a vaguely worded law in Saint Petersburg that came into effect on March 17, 2012, making it a criminal offence to publicize acts of male or female homosexuality, bisexuality, or transgenderism. The intention of the law is to protect minors. A Russian travel advisory on the Foreign Affairs website notes that while homosexuality is legal in Russia (it was decriminalized in 1993), LGBT Canadian travellers should avoid "displaying affection in public, as homosexuals can be targets of violence.... Public actions (including dissemination of information, statements, displays or conspicuous behaviour) contradicting or appearing to contradict this law may lead to arrest, prosecution and the imposition of a fine."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">
        Milan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">
        Venice
       </a>
       were formerly twin cities of Saint Petersburg, but suspended this link due to St Petersburg's ban on "gay propaganda".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
        <a href="#cite_note-168">
         [168]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Milan suspended the relationship with Saint Petersburg on November 23, 2012
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
        <a href="#cite_note-169">
         [169]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Venice did so on January 28, 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
        <a href="#cite_note-170">
         [170]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

           <a class="external text" href="http://translate.google.com/translate?hl=en&amp;sl=ru&amp;tl=en&amp;u=http://www.consultant.ru/cons/cgi/online.cgi?req=doc&amp;base=LAW&amp;n=201180" rel="nofollow">
            On Calculating Time
           </a>
          </i>
          , as amended by the Federal Law #271-FZ of July 03, 2016
          <i>
           On Amending Federal Law "On Calculating Time"
          </i>
          . Effective as of after sixty days following the day of the official publication.).
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-Russian-8">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Official throughout the Russian Federation according to Article 68.1 of the
          <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">
           Constitution of Russia
          </a>
          .
